href="/wiki/ONS_coding_system" title="ONS coding system">ONS code</a></th><td>\nE12000006</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eelga.gov.uk/">www<wbr />.eelga<wbr />.gov<wbr />.uk</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>East of England</b> is one of nine official <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_England" title="Regions of England">regions of England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/First_level_NUTS_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="First level NUTS of the European Union">first level</a> of <a href="/wiki/NUTS_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="NUTS of the United Kingdom">NUTS</a> for <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">statistical</a> purposes. It was created in 1994 and was adopted for statistics from 1999. It includes the ceremonial counties of <a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire" title="Bedfordshire">Bedfordshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire" title="Cambridgeshire">Cambridgeshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suffolk" title="Suffolk">Suffolk</a>. <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a> has the highest population in the region.\n</p><p>Its population at the 2011 census was 5,847,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Region_populations_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Region_populations-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> \n<a href="/wiki/Bedford" title="Bedford">Bedford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwich" title="Norwich">Norwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipswich" title="Ipswich">Ipswich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colchester" title="Colchester">Colchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a> are the region\'s most populous towns. The southern part of the region lies in the <a href="/wiki/London_commuter_belt" title="London commuter belt">London commuter belt</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The region has the lowest elevation range in the UK. North Cambridgeshire and the Essex Coast have most of the around 5% of the region which is below 10 metres above sea level. <a href="/wiki/The_Fens" title="The Fens">The Fens</a> are partly in North Cambridgeshire which is notable for the lowest point in the country in the land of the village of <a href="/wiki/Holme,_Cambridgeshire" title="Holme, Cambridgeshire">Holme</a> 2.75 metres (9.0&#160;ft) below mean sea level which was once <a href="/wiki/Whittlesey_Mere" title="Whittlesey Mere">Whittlesey Mere</a>. The highest point is at Clipper Down at 817&#160;ft (249&#160;m), in the far south-western corner of the region in the Ivinghoe Hills.\n</p><p>Basildon and Harlow (Essex), with Stevenage and Hemel Hempstead (Hertfordshire), were main <a href="/wiki/New_towns_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="New towns in the United Kingdom">New Towns</a> in the 1950s and 1960s, with much industry located there; three of these are on motorways, and fairly equidistant from London. In the late 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Roskill_Commission" title="Roskill Commission">Roskill Commission</a> considered <a href="/wiki/Thurleigh" title="Thurleigh">Thurleigh</a> in Bedfordshire, <a href="/wiki/Nuthampstead" title="Nuthampstead">Nuthampstead</a> in Hertfordshire and <a href="/wiki/Foulness" class="mw-redirect" title="Foulness">Foulness</a> in Essex as a possible <a href="/wiki/London%27s_third_airport_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="London&#39;s third airport (disambiguation)">third airport for London</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_use">Historical use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Historical use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table of political science">Other countries</a></li>\n<li><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_England" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of England">Atlas</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_England&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The East of England succeeded the  <a href="/wiki/Standard_statistical_regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard statistical regions">standard statistical region</a> East Anglia (excluding <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire" title="Bedfordshire">Bedfordshire</a> then in the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a>). The East of England <a href="/wiki/Historical_and_alternative_regions_of_England#Civil_defence_regions" title="Historical and alternative regions of England">civil defence region</a> was identical to today\'s region.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Anglia_and_overlap_with_Home_Counties">East Anglia and overlap with Home Counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: East Anglia and overlap with Home Counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>England between the Wash and just south of the town of <a href="/wiki/Colchester" title="Colchester">Colchester</a> has since post-Roman times (6th century) been and continues to be known as <a href="/wiki/East_Anglia" title="East Anglia">East Anglia</a>, including the county traversing the west of this line, <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire" title="Cambridgeshire">Cambridgeshire</a>. The inclusion of Essex as part of East Anglia is open to debate, notably because it was a Saxon kingdom, separate from the kingdom of the East Angles.\n</p><p>Essex, despite meaning East-Saxons, previously formed part of the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East England</a>, as did Bedfordshire and Hertfordshire, a mixture of definite and debatable <a href="/wiki/Home_Counties" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Counties">Home Counties</a>.  The earliest use of the term is from 1695. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Davenant" title="Charles Davenant">Charles Davenant</a>, in <i>An essay upon ways and means of supplying the war</i>, wrote, "The Eleven Home Counties, which are thought in Land Taxes to pay more than their proportion..." then cited a list including these four.  The term does not appear to have been used in taxation since the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>East Anglia is one of the driest parts of the United Kingdom with average rainfall ranging from 450&#160;mm to 750&#160;mm. This is usually because <a href="/wiki/Low_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Low pressure">low pressure</a> systems and <a href="/wiki/Weather_front" title="Weather front">weather fronts</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> have lost a lot of their moisture over land (and therefore are usually a lot weaker) by the time they reach Eastern England.  However <a href="/wiki/The_Fens" title="The Fens">the Fens</a> in Cambridgeshire are prone to flooding should a strong system affect the area.\n</p><p>Winter (mid November \xe2\x80\x93 mid March) is mostly cool but non-prevailing cold easterly winds can affect the area from the continent, these can bring heavy snowfall if the winds interact with a <a href="/wiki/Low_pressure_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Low pressure system">low pressure system</a> over the Atlantic or <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. Northerly winds can also be cold but are not usually as cold as easterly winds. Westerly winds bring milder and, typically, wetter weather. Southerly winds usually bring mild air (if from the Atlantic or <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>) but chill if coming from further east than Spain.\n</p><p>Spring (mid March \xe2\x80\x93 May) is a transitional season that can be chilly to start with but is usually warm by late-April/May. The weather at this time is often changeable (within each day) and occasionally showery.\n</p><p>Summer (June \xe2\x80\x93 mid September) is usually warm and continental air from mainland Europe or the <a href="/wiki/Azores_High" title="Azores High">Azores High</a> usually leads to at least a few weeks of hot, balmy weather with prolonged warm to hot weather. The number of summer storms from the Atlantic, such as the remnants of a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> usually coincides with the location of the <a href="/wiki/Jet_stream" title="Jet stream">jet stream</a>. The East tends to receive much less of their rain than the other regions.\n</p><p>Autumn (mid September \xe2\x80\x93 mid November) is usually mild with some days being very unsettled and rainy and others warm. At least part of September and early October in the East have warm and settled weather but only in rare years is there an <a href="/wiki/Indian_summer" title="Indian summer">Indian summer</a> where fine weather marks the entire traditional harvest season.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deprivation">Deprivation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Deprivation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The most deprived districts, according to the <a href="/wiki/Indices_of_deprivation_2007" title="Indices of deprivation 2007">Indices of deprivation 2007</a> in the region are, in descending order, Great Yarmouth (58th in England), Norwich (62nd), <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a> (87th), Peterborough (90th) and <a href="/wiki/Ipswich" title="Ipswich">Ipswich</a> (99th). At county level, after Luton and Peterborough, which have a similar level of deprivation, in descending order there is <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> then <a href="/wiki/Thurrock" title="Thurrock">Thurrock</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The least deprived districts, in descending order, are South Cambridgeshire, Uttlesford, Mid Bedfordshire, East Hertfordshire, St Albans, Brentwood, Rochford, Chelmsford, Huntingdonshire, Mid Suffolk, Broadland, North Hertfordshire, Dacorum, Three Rivers, South Norfolk, East Cambridgeshire and Suffolk Coastal. At county level, the least deprived areas in the region, in descending order, are Cambridgeshire, Hertfordshire and Bedfordshire, with all three having a similar level of deprivation, then Essex.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region has the lowest proportion of jobless households in the UK \xe2\x80\x93 0.5%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In March 2011 the region\'s <a href="/wiki/Jobseeker%27s_Allowance" title="Jobseeker&#39;s Allowance">unemployment claimant</a> count was 3.0%. Inside the region, the highest rate is <a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Yarmouth (borough)">Great Yarmouth</a> with 6.2%, followed by Peterborough, Ipswich and <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> on 4.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_(East_of_England).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28East_of_England%29.svg/220px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28East_of_England%29.svg.png" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28East_of_England%29.svg/330px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28East_of_England%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28East_of_England%29.svg/440px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28East_of_England%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="947" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_(East_of_England).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General Election results in 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 2015 general election, there was an overall swing of 0.25% from the Conservatives to Labour, and the Liberal Democrats lost 16% of its vote. All of Hertfordshire and Suffolk is now Conservative. The region\'s electorate voted 49% Conservative, 22% Labour, 16% UKIP, 8% Liberal Democrat and 4% Green. Like other regions, the division of seats favours the dominant party in the region, and the Conservatives have 52, Labour 4 (<a href="/wiki/Cambridge_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cambridge (UK Parliament constituency)">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Luton South (UK Parliament constituency)">Luton South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton_North_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Luton North (UK Parliament constituency)">Luton North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Norwich South (UK Parliament constituency)">Norwich South</a>), UKIP 1 (<a href="/wiki/Clacton_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Clacton (UK Parliament constituency)">Clacton</a>) and 1 Liberal Democrat (<a href="/wiki/North_Norfolk_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Norfolk (UK Parliament constituency)">North Norfolk</a>).\n</p>\n<div role="navigation" class="navbox" href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a> CC\n</td>\n<td>UKH33\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_government">Regional government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Regional government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An <a href="/wiki/East_of_England_Regional_Strategy_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="East of England Regional Strategy Board">East of England Regional Strategy Board</a> exists to co-ordinate the work of the local councils in the area and provides other functions.  It is based in <a href="/wiki/Flempton" title="Flempton">Flempton</a> on the A1101 north-west of <a href="/wiki/Bury_St_Edmunds" title="Bury St Edmunds">Bury St Edmunds</a>.  The Government shut the Government office for the East of England in 2011, the <a href="/wiki/East_of_England_Development_Agency" title="East of England Development Agency">East of England Development Agency</a> is being closed also.  The East of England also elects MEPs for the <a href="/wiki/East_of_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="East of England (European Parliament constituency)">East of England (European Parliament constituency)</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_of_England_Plan">East of England Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: East of England Plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The current version of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England_Plan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="East of England Plan (page does not exist)">East of England Plan</a>, a revision of the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Spatial_Strategy" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Spatial Strategy">Regional Spatial Strategy</a> for the East of England, was published on 12 May 2008.  It was revoked on 3 January 2013<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The official <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_England" title="Regions of England">region</a> consists of the following subdivisions:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Map</th>\n<th>Ceremonial county</th>\n<th>Shire county / unitary</th>\n<th>Districts\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="11"><a
