href="/wiki/Fenland_District" title="Fenland District">Fenland</a>, <i>e</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/East_Cambridgeshire" title="East Cambridgeshire">East Cambridgeshire</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">9.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a> U.A.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">10.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a></td>\n<td><i>a</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Norwich" title="Norwich">Norwich</a>, <i>b</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/South_Norfolk" title="South Norfolk">South Norfolk</a>, <i>c</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth" title="Great Yarmouth">Great Yarmouth</a>, <i>d</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Broadland" title="Broadland">Broadland</a>, <i>e</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/North_Norfolk" title="North Norfolk">North Norfolk</a>, <i>f</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Breckland_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Breckland (district)">Breckland</a>, <i>g</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn_and_West_Norfolk" title="King&#39;s Lynn and West Norfolk">King\'s Lynn and West Norfolk</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">11.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Suffolk" title="Suffolk">Suffolk</a></td>\n<td><i>a</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Ipswich_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ipswich (borough)">Ipswich</a>, <i>b</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Suffolk_Coastal" title="Suffolk Coastal">Suffolk Coastal</a>, <i>c</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Waveney_District" title="Waveney District">Waveney</a>, <i>d</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Mid_Suffolk" title="Mid Suffolk">Mid Suffolk</a>, <i>e</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Babergh" title="Babergh">Babergh</a>, <i>f</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/St_Edmundsbury_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="St Edmundsbury (borough)">St. Edmundsbury</a>, <i>g</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Forest_Heath" title="Forest Heath">Forest Heath</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/West_Runton_Elephant" class="mw-redirect" title="West Runton Elephant">mammoth skeleton</a> found at <a href="/wiki/West_Runton" title="West Runton">West Runton</a>, Norfolk, in 1990, is the most complete in the world. <a href="/wiki/Happisburgh_footprints" title="Happisburgh footprints">Fossilised footprints</a> discovered on a nearby beach in 2010 at <a href="/wiki/Happisburgh" title="Happisburgh">Happisburgh</a> are 900,000 years old, and the oldest evidence of early humans outside of Africa, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_antecessor" title="Homo antecessor">Homo antecessor</a></i>, with the earliest flint hand axe in north-west Europe..\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Simon_Sudbury" title="Simon Sudbury">Simon Sudbury</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a> from 1375\xe2\x80\x9381, introduced the Poll Tax in Sudbury in the 1300s and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants\' Revolt</a> in Essex in May 1381 was led by <a href="/wiki/Wat_Tyler" title="Wat Tyler">Wat Tyler</a>. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Garrett_Anderson" title="Elizabeth Garrett Anderson">Elizabeth Garrett Anderson</a>, from Suffolk, qualified as Britain\'s first female doctor in 1865, and was the granddaughter of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Garrett_(1755%E2%80%931839)" title="Richard Garrett (1755\xe2\x80\x931839)">Richard Garrett</a>, whose company produced some of the first steam-powered road vehicles. On 3 October 1959 postcodes were introduced in the UK at Norwich only; Norwich was the first main town in the UK to be pedestrianised in 1967. The <a href="/wiki/Access_(credit_card)" title="Access (credit card)">Access</a> <a href="/wiki/Credit_card" title="Credit card">credit card</a> was introduced in October 1972 from Southend. King\'s Lynn was the first in the UK to install a town-centre CCTV system, from 1987.\n</p><p>Britain\'s first self-service petrol station was opened on 24 March 1966 on <a href="/wiki/Marshalswick" title="Marshalswick">Marshalswick</a> Lane in St Albans by <a href="/wiki/Heron_International" title="Heron International">Heron</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_and_the_Protectorate">Civil War and the Protectorate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Civil War and the Protectorate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The East of England was a major force and resource for Parliament, and in particular in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association" title="Eastern Association">Eastern Association</a>. <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> came from Huntingdon.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Norfolk, Suffolk and Essex played host to the American <a href="/wiki/VIII_Bomber_Command" class="mw-redirect" title="VIII Bomber Command">VIII Bomber Command</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Air_Force" title="Ninth Air Force">Ninth Air Force</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_War_Museum_Duxford" title="Imperial War Museum Duxford">Imperial War Museum at Duxford</a> has an exhibition, commemorating their participation and sacrifice, near to the M11 south of Cambridge.\n</p><p>Stansted Airport was <a href="/wiki/RAF_Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="RAF Stansted Mountfitchet">RAF Stansted Mountfitchet</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/344th_Bombardment_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="344th Bombardment Group">344th Bombardment Group</a>. The <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Mosquito" title="De Havilland Mosquito">de Havilland Mosquito</a> was mainly assembled at Hatfield and Leavesden, although much of the innovative wooden structure originated outside the region from the furniture industry of <a href="/wiki/High_Wycombe" title="High Wycombe">High Wycombe</a>; the Mosquito entered service in 1942 with <a href="/wiki/No._105_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 105 Squadron RAF">105 Sqn</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Horsham_St_Faith" title="RAF Horsham St Faith">RAF Horsham St Faith</a>. <a href="/wiki/RAF_Tempsford" title="RAF Tempsford">RAF Tempsford</a> in Bedford is the airfield from where <a href="/wiki/Special_Operations_Executive" title="Special Operations Executive">SOE</a> secret agents for Europe took off, with <a href="/wiki/No._138_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 138 Squadron RAF">138 Sqn</a> which parachuted agents and equipment and <a href="/wiki/No._161_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 161 Squadron RAF">161 Sqn</a> which landed and retrieved agents. <a href="/wiki/No._19_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 19 Squadron RAF">19 Sqn</a> at Duxford was the first to be equipped with the Spitfire on 4 August 1938.\n</p><p>Rudimentary <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drone technology</a> was developed by the USAF at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Fersfield" title="RAF Fersfield">RAF Fersfield</a>, to destroy the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Mimoyecques" title="Fortress of Mimoyecques">Fortress of Mimoyecques</a> at <a href="/wiki/Moyecques" title="Moyecques">Moyecques</a>; a prototype drone aircraft of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Aphrodite" title="Operation Aphrodite">Operation Aphrodite</a>, with <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>\'s older brother <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kennedy,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph P. Kennedy, Jr.">Joseph P. Kennedy, Jr.</a> aboard, exploded on 12 August 1944 over the <a href="/wiki/River_Blyth,_Suffolk" title="River Blyth, Suffolk">Blyth estuary</a> in Suffolk.\n</p><p>A magnetic mine found in 1939 at <a href="/wiki/Shoeburyness" title="Shoeburyness">Shoeburyness</a>, now in Southend, allowed the German magnetic <a href="/wiki/Naval_mine" title="Naval mine">mine</a> threat to be subdued, with work done at <a href="/wiki/HMS_Vernon_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Vernon (shore establishment)">HMS Vernon</a> in Portsmouth.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Forces_in_Europe_-_Air_Forces_Africa" title="United States Air Forces in Europe - Air Forces Africa">United States Air Forces in Europe - Air Forces Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="United States Air Force in the United Kingdom">United States Air Force in the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/81st_Training_Wing" title="81st Training Wing">81st Tactical Fighter Wing</a> were at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Bentwaters" title="RAF Bentwaters">RAF Bentwaters</a> from January 1952, and also at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Woodbridge" title="RAF Woodbridge">RAF Woodbridge</a>; in the late 1980s some of the aircraft went to <a href="/wiki/RAF_Alconbury" title="RAF Alconbury">RAF Alconbury</a>. Alconbury closed in 1992, and Bentwaters closed in 1993, with the American air forces being in the area for 42 years; the USAF aircraft subsequently moved to <a href="/wiki/Spangdahlem_Air_Base" title="Spangdahlem Air Base">Spangdahlem Air Base</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>, Germany.\n</p><p>At <a href="/wiki/RAF_Marham" title="RAF Marham">RAF Marham</a> in west Norfolk, <a href="/wiki/No._214_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 214 Squadron RAF">214 Sqn</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Valiant" title="Vickers Valiant">Vickers Valiant</a> developed the RAF\'s refuelling system; later the squadron would be equipped with the <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page_Victor" title="Handley Page Victor">Handley Page Victor</a>. Work on refuelling had also taken place at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Tarrant_Rushton" title="RAF Tarrant Rushton">RAF Tarrant Rushton</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a>.\n</p><p>From the 1950s, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Wyton" title="RAF Wyton">RAF Wyton</a> was an important reconnaissance base for the RAF, mainly <a href="/wiki/No._543_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 543 Squadron RAF">543 Sqn</a>. The base is now home of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Intelligence_Fusion_Centre" title="Defence Intelligence Fusion Centre">Defence Intelligence Fusion Centre</a>, previously known as JARIC, or the Joint Air Reconnaissance Intelligence Centre from 1956.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_heritage">Scientific heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Scientific heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/James_D._Watson" class="mw-redirect" title="James D. Watson">Watson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick" title="Francis Crick">Crick</a> discovered the <a href="/wiki/Base_pair" title="Base pair">structure</a> of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> at Cambridge on 28 February 1953. <a href="/wiki/William_Bateson" title="William Bateson">William Bateson</a>, at Cambridge, invented the term <i>genetics</i> and co-discovered <a href="/wiki/Genetic_linkage" title="Genetic linkage">genetic linkage</a> with <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Punnett" title="Reginald Punnett">Reginald Punnett</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit,_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit%2C_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg/220px-Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit%2C_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit%2C_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg/330px-Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit%2C_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit%2C_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg/440px-Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit%2C_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glaxo_Smith_Kline_research_unit,_Harlow_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1444766.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GSK in Harlow in August 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Bourn_Hall_Clinic" title="Bourn Hall Clinic">Bourn Hall Clinic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bourn" title="Bourn">Bourn</a>, west of Cambridge, <a href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation" title="In vitro fertilisation">in vitro fertilisation</a> (IVF) was first achieved in 1978. Smith, Kline and French developed <a href="/wiki/Cimetidine" title="Cimetidine">Tagamet</a> in the 1970s at <a href="/wiki/The_Frythe" title="The Frythe">the Frythe</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Welwyn" title="Welwyn">Welwyn</a>; the site was sold by <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GSK</a> in December 2010, and in World War II was home to <a href="/wiki/Station_IX" title="Station IX">Station IX</a>, which made sabotage equipment for secret agents. Tagamet was for many years the world\'s best-selling prescription drug - for <a href="/wiki/Peptic_ulcer" class="mw-redirect" title="Peptic ulcer">stomach ulcers</a>; the team had been led by <a href="/wiki/C._Robin_Ganellin" title="C. Robin Ganellin">C. Robin Ganellin</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Graham_Durant&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Graham Durant (page does not exist)">Graham Durant</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Emmett&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Emmett (page does not exist)">John Emmett</a>. In 1912 in Cambridge <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Gowland_Hopkins" title="Frederick Gowland Hopkins">Frederick Gowland Hopkins</a> discovered vitamins, gaining the Nobel Prize for Medicine in 1929. Under Sir <a href="/wiki/David_Jack_(scientist)" title="David Jack (scientist)">David Jack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allen_%26_Hanburys" title="Allen &amp; Hanburys">Allen &amp; Hanburys</a> at Ware (part of Glaxo Group Research since 1958, next to <a href="/wiki/Chauncy_School" title="Chauncy School">Chauncy School</a>) developed <a href="/wiki/Salbutamol" title="Salbutamol">Ventolin</a> (for asthma) in the late 1960s and <a href="/wiki/Ranitidine" title="Ranitidine">Zantac</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Peptic_ulcer" class="mw-redirect" title="Peptic ulcer">peptic ulcers</a>) in the late 1970s; Zantac was the first pharmaceutical to sell more than $1bn per year; more recently <a href="/wiki/Fluticasone/salmeterol" class="mw-redirect" title="Fluticasone/salmeterol">Seretid</a> (also for asthma) was developed there and the site is now part of GSK, which has a separate manufacturing site there. In 1975 at Cambridge <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Milstein" title="C\xc3\xa9sar Milstein">C\xc3\xa9sar Milstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georges_J._F._K%C3%B6hler" title="Georges J. F. K\xc3\xb6hler">Georges J. F. K\xc3\xb6hler</a> separated <a href="/wiki/Monoclonal_antibodies" class="mw-redirect" title="Monoclonal antibodies">monoclonal antibodies</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(United_Kingdom)" title="Medical Research Council (United Kingdom)">MRC</a> <a href="/wiki/Laboratory_of_Molecular_Biology" title="Laboratory of Molecular Biology">Laboratory of Molecular Biology</a>, and gained the 1984 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize for Medicine</a>; the MRC LMB has had many Nobel prizes for Medicine. <a href="/wiki/Adalimumab" title="Adalimumab">Adalimumab</a>, known as Humira, the world\'s best-selling drug, was partly developed in Cambridge by <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Antibody_Technology" title="Cambridge Antibody Technology">Cambridge Antibody Technology</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Smith_%26_Nephew_Research&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Smith &amp; Nephew Research (page does not exist)">Smith &amp; Nephew Research</a> was based at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gilston_Park_House&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gilston Park House (page does not exist)">Gilston Park House</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Gilston" title="Gilston">Gilston</a>, north of Harlow.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall,_Cambridge,_UK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall%2C_Cambridge%2C_UK.jpg/220px-Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall%2C_Cambridge%2C_UK.jpg" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall%2C_Cambridge%2C_UK.jpg/330px-Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall%2C_Cambridge%2C_UK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall%2C_Cambridge%2C_UK.jpg/440px-Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall%2C_Cambridge%2C_UK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5434" data-file-height="2227" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanger_Institute_and_Hinxton_Hall,_Cambridge,_UK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sanger_sequencing" title="Sanger sequencing">Sanger Institute</a> and Hinxton Hall, off the Stump Cross Interchange of the M11 (J9), home of the Wellcome Genome Campus and the European Bioinformatics Institute, which houses the <a href="/wiki/European_Nucleotide_Archive" title="European Nucleotide Archive">European Nucleotide Archive</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At <a href="/wiki/Papworth_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Papworth Hospital">Papworth Hospital</a> the UK\'s first <a href="/wiki/Heart_transplantation" title="Heart transplantation">heart transplant</a> took place in January 1979, being operated by Sir <a href="/wiki/Terence_English" title="Terence English">Terence English</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Roy_Yorke_Calne" title="Roy Yorke Calne">Roy Calne</a>, on 44-year-old Charles McHugh. The world\'s first heart, lung and liver transplant was performed there on 17 December 1986. The world\'s first long-term <a href="/wiki/Artificial_heart" title="Artificial heart">artificial heart</a> was implanted (and connected) on 26 August 1994 - by Dr <a href="/wiki/John_Wallwork_(surgeon)" title="John Wallwork (surgeon)">John Wallwork</a>; the patient lived for 9 months; John Wallwork had performed Europe\'s first <a href="/wiki/Heart%E2%80%93lung_transplant" title="Heart\xe2\x80\x93lung transplant">heart\xe2\x80\x93lung transplant</a> there in 1984; such transplants are often carried out on people with <a href="/wiki/Cystic_fibrosis" title="Cystic fibrosis">cystic fibrosis</a>. <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Milstein" title="Benjamin Milstein">Ben Milstein</a> conducted Britain\'s first <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_surgery" title="Cardiac surgery">open-heart surgery</a> there in September 1958 on a woman with an <a href="/wiki/Atrial_septal_defect" title="Atrial septal defect">atrial septal defect</a>, known as a <i>hole in the heart</i>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Ray" title="John Ray">John Ray</a> was an important naturalist from Essex, and the first to distinguish <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> between <a href="/wiki/Monocotyledon" title="Monocotyledon">monocotyledons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dicotyledon" title="Dicotyledon">dicotyledons</a> in his 1682 book <i>Methodus Plantarum Nova</i>. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Townshend,_2nd_Viscount_Townshend" title="Charles Townshend, 2nd Viscount Townshend">Charles Townshend, 2nd Viscount Townshend</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Raynham_Hall" title="Raynham Hall">Raynham Hall</a> in Norfolk, introduced <a href="/wiki/Crop_rotation" title="Crop rotation">crop rotation</a> to Britain (which had originated in Holland) in the early 1700s using <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turnip" title="Turnip">turnips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clover" title="Clover">clover</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Maris_Piper" title="Maris Piper">Maris Piper</a> <a href="/wiki/Disease_resistance_in_fruit_and_vegetables" title="Disease resistance in fruit and vegetables">disease-resistant</a> potato was developed by the <a href="/wiki/Plant_Breeding_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Plant Breeding Institute">Plant Breeding Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Trumpington,_Cambridgeshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Trumpington, Cambridgeshire">Trumpington</a> in 1966. At the <a href="/wiki/Rothamsted_Experimental_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Rothamsted Experimental Station">Rothamsted Experimental Station</a>, near Harpenden in Hertfordshire, <a href="/wiki/2,4-Dichlorophenoxyacetic_acid" title="2,4-Dichlorophenoxyacetic acid">2,4-D</a> was discovered, under <a href="/wiki/Juda_Hirsch_Quastel" title="Juda Hirsch Quastel">Juda Hirsch Quastel</a>; this is the most widely used herbicide in the world; later at the station, the <a href="/wiki/Pyrethroid" title="Pyrethroid">pyrethroid</a> insecticide was developed, under Michael Elliott, which is now the most common insecticide on the domestic market.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Gilbert_(astronomer)" title="William Gilbert (astronomer)">William Gilbert (astronomer)</a> from Colchester was an important early physicist; the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_(unit)" title="Gilbert (unit)">Gilbert</a> was a former unit of <a href="/wiki/Magnetization" title="Magnetization">magnetization</a>. <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">Radar</a> was <a href="/wiki/History_of_radar" title="History of radar">developed</a> in around <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford</a> in the late 1930s and at <a href="/wiki/Bawdsey_Manor" title="Bawdsey Manor">Bawdsey Manor</a> on the Suffolk coast; on 24 July 1935 at Orfordness was the first detection on a <a href="/wiki/Cathode_ray_tube" title="Cathode ray tube">CRT</a> screen of tracking a plane on radar - a <a href="/wiki/Westland_Wallace" title="Westland Wallace">Westland Wallace</a>. Earlier radio had been developed around Chelmsford by the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Company" title="Marconi Company">Marconi Company</a>; much of Britain\'s electronics industry was derived from Marconi, later to be GEC and now <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>. In 1864 <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a> at Cambridge discovered his <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_wave_equation" title="Electromagnetic wave equation">electromagnetic wave equation</a>, part of his <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_equations" title="Maxwell&#39;s equations">Maxwell\'s equations</a>. <a href="/wiki/CSR_(company)" title="CSR (company)">CSR</a> (previously Cambridge Silicon Radio) has made much technology for <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">Bluetooth</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BAS_hq1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/BAS_hq1.jpg/220px-BAS_hq1.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/BAS_hq1.jpg/330px-BAS_hq1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/BAS_hq1.jpg/440px-BAS_hq1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BAS_hq1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Antarctic Survey in Cambridge</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/William_Hyde_Wollaston" title="William Hyde Wollaston">William Hyde Wollaston</a>, a chemist from Norfolk, discovered <a href="/wiki/Palladium" title="Palladium">palladium</a> in 1802 and <a href="/wiki/Rhodium" title="Rhodium">rhodium</a> in 1804, and in 1802 discovered\nthe features of the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>\'s electromagnetic spectrum, known as <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_lines" title="Fraunhofer lines">Fraunhofer lines</a>, allowing the chemical composition of the\nSun to be determined. In 1938 at Cambridge, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Cartwright" title="Mary Cartwright">Mary Cartwright</a> developed <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaos theory</a> with <a href="/wiki/John_Edensor_Littlewood" title="John Edensor Littlewood">John Edensor Littlewood</a>; <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton_Lorenz" title="Edward Norton Lorenz">Edward Norton Lorenz</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorologist</a> from the USA, would mainly develop chaos theory in 1963, and the <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_effect" title="Butterfly effect">butterfly effect</a> in 1969. In the 1960s at Cambridge, the <a href="/wiki/Scanning_electron_microscope" title="Scanning electron microscope">scanning electron microscope</a> was developed by Sir <a href="/wiki/Charles_Oatley" title="Charles Oatley">Charles Oatley</a>, and first made by the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Scientific_Instrument_Company" title="Cambridge Scientific Instrument Company">Cambridge Scientific Instrument Company</a> in 1965. In 1966, Cambridge geophysicists <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Vine" title="Frederick Vine">Frederick Vine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drummond_Matthews" title="Drummond Matthews">Drummond Matthews</a> proved the theory of <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">plate tectonics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_drift" title="Continental drift">continental drift</a>; plate tectonics was first suggested at Cambridge by <a href="/wiki/Dan_McKenzie_(geophysicist)" title="Dan McKenzie (geophysicist)">Dan McKenzie</a>; continental drift had first been proposed, though not extensively proved, by the German <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Wegener" title="Alfred Wegener">Alfred Wegener</a> in 1912.  In 1985, Norwich\'s <a href="/wiki/Joe_Farman" title="Joe Farman">Joe Farman</a> discovered the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">hole</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">Ozone layer</a>, when part of Cambridge\'s <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Survey" title="British Antarctic Survey">British Antarctic Survey</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Cockcroft" title="John Cockcroft">John Cockcroft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Walton" title="Ernest Walton">Ernest Walton</a>, using a <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">particle-accelerator</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Cockcroft%E2%80%93Walton_generator" title="Cockcroft\xe2\x80\x93Walton generator">Cockcroft\xe2\x80\x93Walton generator</a> performed the first artificial <a href="/wiki/Decay_chain" title="Decay chain">nuclear disintegration</a> on 14 April 1932, with a <a href="/wiki/Charged_particle_beam" title="Charged particle beam">proton beam</a> on lithium (producing helium) at the Cavendish Laboratory; using this work on 12 September 1933 the Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3_Szil%C3%A1rd" class="mw-redirect" title="Le\xc3\xb3 Szil\xc3\xa1rd">Le\xc3\xb3 Szil\xc3\xa1rd</a> would conceive the idea of the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_chain_reaction" title="Nuclear chain reaction">nuclear chain reaction</a> whilst standing at a set of traffic lights on <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Row" title="Southampton Row">Southampton Row</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury" title="Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury</a>, returning from a lecture by <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a> which discussed <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a> 1914 book <a href="/wiki/The_World_Set_Free" title="The World Set Free">The World Set Free</a>, that overtly prophecised nuclear weapons. The <a href="/wiki/Cavendish_Laboratory" title="Cavendish Laboratory">Cavendish Laboratory</a> has 29 Nobel prize winners, more than anywhere else, and many Western countries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_heritage">Industrial heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Industrial heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_Sign,_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Road_Sign%2C_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg/250px-Road_Sign%2C_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Road_Sign%2C_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg/375px-Road_Sign%2C_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Road_Sign%2C_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg/500px-Road_Sign%2C_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_Sign,_Chelmsford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_418434.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chelmsford is the birthplace of radio</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ransomes,_Sims_%26_Jefferies" title="Ransomes, Sims &amp; Jefferies">Ransomes, Sims &amp; Jefferies</a> of Ipswich built the first engine-powered commercial lawnmower in 1902. The firm would later own <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mountfield_(lawn_mowers)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mountfield (lawn mowers) (page does not exist)">Mountfield</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chorleywood_bread_process" title="Chorleywood bread process">Chorleywood bread process</a> from 1961 changed bread production all over world. <a href="/wiki/John_Dickinson_Stationery" title="John Dickinson Stationery">John Dickinson Stationery</a> of Hertfordshire was the first company to produce <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamp_gum" title="Postage stamp gum">gummed</a> envelopes in 1850, and <a href="/wiki/Windowed_envelope" title="Windowed envelope">windowed envelopes</a> in 1929 (in production quantities). The <a href="/wiki/Thursford_Collection" title="Thursford Collection">Thursford Collection</a> in Norfolk is  the country\'s biggest collection of steam engines.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_radio" title="History of radio">History of radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_broadcasting" title="History of broadcasting">History of broadcasting</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Company" title="Marconi Company">Marconi Company</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/New_Street_Works" title="New Street Works">New Street Works</a> on the B1008 in Chelmsford was the world\'s first radio factory in 1912; on 15 June 1920, Britain\'s first radio broadcast was made by Dame <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Melba" title="Nellie Melba">Nellie Melba</a>. The first radio broadcast in UK was in December 1919 from Marconi in Chelmsford, broadcasting news for the first time in December 1920. The world\'s first scheduled broadcast from the <a href="/wiki/2MT" title="2MT">2MT</a> (<i>Two Emma Toc</i>) Marconi transmitter at <a href="/wiki/Writtle" title="Writtle">Writtle</a> was from 14 February 1922, only on Tuesday evenings. The world\'s first real-time computer (Type 152) with memory store (<a href="/wiki/Williams_tube" title="Williams tube">Williams tubes</a>) was built in 1947 by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Elliott_Brothers_Research_Laboratories&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Elliott Brothers Research Laboratories (page does not exist)">Elliott Brothers Research Laboratories</a> at Borehamwood; the site became <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Avionics" class="mw-redirect" title="Marconi Avionics">Marconi Avionics</a> in 1978 and <a href="/w/index.php?title=GEC_Avionics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GEC Avionics (page does not exist)">GEC Avionics</a> in 1984, and also had <a href="/wiki/GEC_Computers" title="GEC Computers">GEC Computers</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg/220px-Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg/330px-Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg/440px-Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Orbiter_Structural_Thermal_Model.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Part of the <a href="/wiki/Solar_Orbiter" title="Solar Orbiter">Solar Orbiter</a> being built at Stevenage by <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">Airbus Defence and Space</a> (former Astrium) in March 2015; Hertfordshire built the UK\'s rockets, with Stevenage being the main home of the UK\'s spacecraft</div></div></div>\n<p>Glues for the Mosquito wooden airframe were developed by <a href="/wiki/Norman_de_Bruyne" title="Norman de Bruyne">Norman de Bruyne</a> at his Duxford-based <a href="/wiki/Aero_Research_Limited" title="Aero Research Limited">Aero Research Limited</a>, which invented <a href="/wiki/Araldite" title="Araldite">Araldite</a>; the site is now owned by <a href="/wiki/Hexcel" title="Hexcel">Hexcel</a>. The Mosquito fuselage was made from two halves of balsawood (<a href="/wiki/Ochroma" title="Ochroma">Ochroma</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, and Canadian <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">Birch</a>, which had a <a href="/wiki/Madapolam" title="Madapolam">Madapolam</a> fabric over the surface; the wings were made from <a href="/wiki/Plywood" title="Plywood">plywood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">spruce</a>. De Havilland built the <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Comet" title="De Havilland Comet">Comet</a> (the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Jet_airliner" title="Jet airliner">jet airliner</a>, first flying in July 1949 when piloted by <a href="/wiki/John_Cunningham_(RAF_officer)" title="John Cunningham (RAF officer)">John Cunningham</a>, powered by <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Ghost" title="De Havilland Ghost">DH jet engines</a>, and designed by <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Eric_Bishop" title="Ronald Eric Bishop">R.E. Bishop</a>) at Hatfield, and built the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Streak_(missile)" title="Blue Streak (missile)">Blue Streak</a> rocket launcher at its Stevenage base; by the end of WWII the <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Goblin" title="De Havilland Goblin">DH Goblin</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Halford" title="Frank Halford">Frank Halford</a>, was the world\'s most powerful jet engine. <a href="/wiki/Ball_bearing" title="Ball bearing">Ball bearings</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Merlin" title="Rolls-Royce Merlin">Merlin</a> engine came from <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford#Hoffmann_Ball_Bearings_.28R.H.P..29" title="Chelmsford">Hoffman</a> of Chelmsford; its former site is now the Rivermead university campus. The first <a href="/wiki/Autoland" title="Autoland">autoland</a> system demonstrated on an airliner was with a <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">BEA</a> <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Trident" title="Hawker Siddeley Trident">Trident</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAE_Bedford" title="RAE Bedford">RAE Bedford</a> in March 1964, with a system developed by <a href="/wiki/Smiths_Group" title="Smiths Group">Smiths Industries</a> with similar work also done for the RAF at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Martlesham_Heath" title="RAF Martlesham Heath">RAF Martlesham Heath</a>; Plessey was a world leader in <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">instrument landing systems</a> (ILS). <a href="/wiki/Rex_Pierson" title="Rex Pierson">Rex Pierson</a> from Norfolk, was the main designer for <a href="/wiki/Vickers-Armstrongs" title="Vickers-Armstrongs">Vickers</a> until the 1950s, designing the <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Vimy" title="Vickers Vimy">Vickers Vimy</a> (which <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight_of_Alcock_and_Brown" title="Transatlantic flight of Alcock and Brown">crossed the Atlantic</a> in June 1919) to the <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a>, both pioneering aircraft. From 1945 to 1992, Rolls-Royce designed and built its helicopter (<a href="/wiki/Turboshaft" title="Turboshaft">turboshaft</a>) engines at its Small Engine Division at Leavesden, now a film set, these engines are now built by <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Turbomeca" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce Turbomeca">Rolls-Royce Turbomeca</a> (from 1966). Britain\'s first satellite constructed in the UK - <a href="/wiki/Ariel_3" title="Ariel 3">Ariel 3</a> (originally titled UK-3) - was built at <a href="/wiki/British_Aircraft_Corporation" title="British Aircraft Corporation">BAC</a>\'s Guided Weapon Division in Stevenage in the mid-1960s, later launched in May 1967. The <a href="/wiki/Europa_(rocket)" title="Europa (rocket)">Europa (rocket)</a> was initially mostly British-led by <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Dynamics" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawker Siddeley Dynamics">Hawker Siddeley Dynamics</a> at Stevenage and test-fired at <a href="/wiki/Woomera_Test_Range" class="mw-redirect" title="Woomera Test Range">Woomera Test Range</a> in Australia, but later the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Ariane_(rocket_family)" title="Ariane (rocket family)">Ariane (rocket family)</a> would be mostly French-built and launched at <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">Guiana Space Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>; <a href="/wiki/Arianespace" title="Arianespace">Arianespace</a> is 64% French and 20% German by ownership, and has no British share of ownership. The <a href="/wiki/Rapier_(missile)" title="Rapier (missile)">Rapier (missile)</a> was developed by BAC (guided weapons division) at Stevenage (former English Electric).\n</p><p>The first transition from hover to free flight of the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_P.1127" title="Hawker Siddeley P.1127">Hawker Siddeley P.1127</a> took place on 8 September 1961 at RAE Bedford, with its first conventional flight also there on 13 March 1961; the Harrier was first delivered to RAF Wittering on 18 April 1969 to <a href="/wiki/No._1_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 1 Squadron RAF">1 Squadron</a>; the next squadron to have the Harrier was <a href="/wiki/No._4_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 4 Squadron RAF">4 Sqn</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Wildenrath" title="RAF Wildenrath">RAF Wildenrath</a>. In June 1954, the first <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Aircraft" title="Hunting Aircraft">Hunting Percival</a> <a href="/wiki/BAC_Jet_Provost" title="BAC Jet Provost">Jet Provost</a> flew from Luton Airport; it was the world\'s first-designed jet trainer aircraft. On 30 April 1958, the <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Buccaneer" title="Blackburn Buccaneer">Buccaneer</a> first flew from RAE Bedford. The <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Air_Vehicles_HAV-3" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid Air Vehicles HAV-3">Hybrid Air Vehicles HAV-3</a>, unveiled in 2014 at Cardington, is the longest aircraft in the world. The Comet G-ALYP was the first to enter commercial service for a jet, on 2 May 1952, on a flight from London Airport to Johannesburg; flying back from Rome to London, on a flight from Singapore on 10 January 1954, the aircraft was the second Comet to crash in-flight on <a href="/wiki/BOAC_Flight_781" title="BOAC Flight 781">BOAC Flight 781</a>, and maybe the first to show structural failure; 114 Comets were made. The <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_125" title="British Aerospace 125">British Aerospace 125</a> (DH.125) was the world\'s first business jet, when it first flew in August 1962 at Hatfield, later mostly built at Chester (<a href="/wiki/Hawarden_Airport" title="Hawarden Airport">Broughton</a>); later it evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_800" title="Hawker 800">Hawker 800</a>, made in <a href="/wiki/Wichita,_Kansas" title="Wichita, Kansas">Wichita, Kansas</a>, and the design is the world\'s best selling business jet, with over 1,000 built. The <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300" title="Airbus A300">Airbus A300</a>, which entered service in 1974, started life as the Hawker Siddeley/<a href="/wiki/Breguet_Aviation" title="Breguet Aviation">Breguet</a>/<a href="/wiki/Nord_Aviation" title="Nord Aviation">Nord</a> HBN 100, with much of the initial design produced by Hawker Siddeley from its HS.134 design; the wings were developed from the Trident <a href="/wiki/Supercritical_airfoil" title="Supercritical airfoil">supercritical</a> design (designed in the late 1950s). Of the companies involved with Airbus at the beginning, only Hawker Siddeley (former De Havilland) at Hatfield had designed anything as large with jet engines; the company may have consequently been headquartered at Hatfield and not <a href="/wiki/Toulouse%E2%80%93Blagnac_Airport" title="Toulouse\xe2\x80\x93Blagnac Airport">Toulouse</a>. Today\'s Airbus wings are all made at Broughton in <a href="/wiki/Flintshire" title="Flintshire">Flintshire</a>, and all the undercarriage is made in <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham" title="Cheltenham">Cheltenham</a> (<a href="/wiki/Messier-Bugatti-Dowty" class="mw-redirect" title="Messier-Bugatti-Dowty">Messier-Bugatti-Dowty</a>).\n</p><p>In 1951 on an <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Delay_Storage_Automatic_Calculator" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic Delay Storage Automatic Calculator">EDSAC</a> computer at Cambridge, <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Douglas" title="Sandy Douglas">Sandy Douglas</a> made the world\'s <a href="/wiki/First_video_game" class="mw-redirect" title="First video game">first computer game</a> with a digital graphical display - a version of <i><a href="/wiki/Tic-tac-toe" title="Tic-tac-toe">Noughts and Crosses</a></i>; the <a href="/wiki/LEO_(computer)" title="LEO (computer)">LEO (computer)</a>, the world\'s first commercial computer developed by John Simmons at <a href="/wiki/J._Lyons_and_Co." title="J. Lyons and Co.">J. Lyons and Co.</a>, was a Cambridge EDSAC. <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Research" title="Sinclair Research">Sinclair Research</a> was based in Cambridge, as was its competitor in the 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Acorn_Computers" title="Acorn Computers">Acorn Computers</a>. Sinclair invented the (\xc2\xa380 current value) <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Executive" title="Sinclair Executive">Sinclair Executive</a> in 1972, the world\'s first slimline pocket <a href="/wiki/Calculator" title="Calculator">calculator</a>; then it invented the world\'s first digital <a href="/wiki/Crystal_oscillator" title="Crystal oscillator">quartz</a> <a href="/wiki/Watch" title="Watch">watch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Black_Watch_(wristwatch)" title="Black Watch (wristwatch)">Black Watch</a> (which had technical problems) in 1975. <a href="/wiki/Standard_Telecommunication_Laboratories" title="Standard Telecommunication Laboratories">Standard Telecommunication Laboratories</a> in Harlow, then owned by ITT, is where <a href="/wiki/Fiber-optic_communication" title="Fiber-optic communication">fibre-optic communications</a> as we know today, are recognised as beginning, when developed by <a href="/wiki/George_Hockham" title="George Hockham">George Hockham</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Charles_K._Kao" title="Charles K. Kao">Charles K. Kao</a> (they received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize for Physics</a> in 2009); the first trial cable was laid between Hitchin and Stevenage in 1978. The first optical fibre that was part of a <a href="/wiki/Public_switched_telephone_network" title="Public switched telephone network">public switched telephone network</a> was laid between Martlesham and Ipswich in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Acorn successfully tested its first chip on 26 April 1985 (made in the USA by <a href="/wiki/VLSI_Technology" title="VLSI Technology">VLSI Technology</a>), leading to the <a href="/wiki/Acorn_Archimedes" title="Acorn Archimedes">Acorn Archimedes</a> in 1987, powered by its chip design. Acorn RISC Machines Ltd was formed in 1990, becoming ARM Holdings in 1998, and its <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">chip designs</a> went into all <a href="/wiki/Nokia_phone_series" title="Nokia phone series">Nokia phones</a>, and on <a href="/wiki/Texas_Instruments" title="Texas Instruments">Texas Instruments</a> chips (the <a href="/wiki/Sitara_ARM_Processor" title="Sitara ARM Processor">Sitara processor</a>); currently there are now over 20 billion ARM chips in mobile phones. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vaughan_Programming_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vaughan Programming Services (page does not exist)">Vaughan Programming Services</a> founded by <a href="/wiki/Dina_St_Johnston" title="Dina St Johnston">Dina St Johnston</a> in 1959 in Hertfordshire was Britain\'s first software house.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sizewell_nuclear_power_stations" title="Sizewell nuclear power stations">Sizewell B</a> is Britain\'s only <a href="/wiki/Pressurised_water_reactor" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressurised water reactor">pressurised water reactor</a> (PWR), and is near <a href="/wiki/Leiston" title="Leiston">Leiston</a> in Suffolk with enough power for two million homes; Sizewell A had opened in 1966 and <a href="/wiki/Bradwell_nuclear_power_station" title="Bradwell nuclear power station">Bradwell</a> had opened in 1962. Sir <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Cockerell" title="Christopher Cockerell">Christopher Cockerell</a> (born in Cambridge) developed the hovercraft on <a href="/wiki/Oulton_Broad" title="Oulton Broad">Oulton Broad</a>, Suffolk in 1956. <a href="/wiki/Shell_Haven" title="Shell Haven">Shell Haven</a>, now in Thurrock, was where <a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">bitumen</a> was first ever produced there in 1920; the refinery closed in 1999. Charles Wallace Chapman of <a href="/wiki/Perkins_Engines" title="Perkins Engines">Perkins Engines</a> invented the high speed diesel engine, first building an experimental version (the Vixen) in December 1932 on Queen Street in Peterborough. The world\'s first diesel-engined car, a <a href="/wiki/Hillman_Wizard" title="Hillman Wizard">Hillman Wizard</a> fitted with the engine in March 1933, was tested around Peterborough; the first production engine would be the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Perkins_Wolf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Perkins Wolf (page does not exist)">Perkins Wolf</a>, with the innovative Perkins Aeroflow combustion system; the Perkins Engines company developed mainly from this engine.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1808 <a href="/wiki/Henry_Fourdrinier" title="Henry Fourdrinier">Henry Fourdrinier</a> developed a process at <a href="/wiki/St_Neots" title="St Neots">St Neots</a> to produce continuous rolls of paper, as <a href="/wiki/Paper_machine" title="Paper machine">made today</a>\n- the Fourdrinier Machine, developed with <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Donkin" title="Bryan Donkin">Bryan Donkin</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Crosfield" title="John Crosfield">John Crosfield</a> in Hemel Hempstead invented the colour scanner in 1958. Great Yarmouth\'s <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Sayer" title="Malcolm Sayer">Malcolm Sayer</a> designed the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_E-Type" title="Jaguar E-Type">Jaguar E-Type</a> and initial plans of the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_XJS" title="Jaguar XJS">Jaguar XJS</a>. Captain <a href="/wiki/George_William_Manby" title="George William Manby">George William Manby</a> of Norfolk invented the first portable <a href="/wiki/Fire_extinguisher" title="Fire extinguisher">fire extinguisher</a> in 1813.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The former electricity company for the area, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Electricity" title="Eastern Electricity">Eastern Electricity</a>, has the area\'s distribution now looked after by <a href="/wiki/UK_Power_Networks" title="UK Power Networks">UK Power Networks</a> at Fore Hamlet in <a href="/wiki/Ipswich" title="Ipswich">Ipswich</a>. UK Power Networks also looks after London and most of the South-East. <a href="/wiki/Business_Link" title="Business Link">Business Link</a> in the East of England is next door to the headquarters of T-Mobile UK in Hatfield, at the roundabout of the A1057 and the A1001 on the Bishops Square Business Park.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The region\'s <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_Advisory_Service" title="Manufacturing Advisory Service">Manufacturing Advisory Service</a> is at <a href="/wiki/Melbourn" title="Melbourn">Melbourn</a> in Cambridgeshire, off the <a href="/wiki/A10_road_(England)" title="A10 road (England)">A10</a> and north of <a href="/wiki/Royston,_Hertfordshire" title="Royston, Hertfordshire">Royston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UK_Trade_%26_Investment" title="UK Trade &amp; Investment">UKTI</a> for the region is in <a href="/wiki/Histon_and_Impington" title="Histon and Impington">Histon</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> with its international trade team based next to <a href="/wiki/Magdalene_College,_Cambridge" title="Magdalene College, Cambridge">Magdalene College</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/NHS_East_of_England" title="NHS East of England">NHS East of England</a>, which was the <a href="/wiki/NHS_strategic_health_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="NHS strategic health authority">strategic health authority</a> for the area until the abolition of these areas in 2013, is on Capital Park, next to <a href="/wiki/Fulbourn" title="Fulbourn">Fulbourn</a> Tesco, <a href="/wiki/Fulbourn_Hospital" title="Fulbourn Hospital">Fulbourn Hospital</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_to_Ely_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Ipswich to Ely Line">Cambridge-Ipswich railway</a>, on the eastern edge of Cambridge. The <a href="/wiki/East_of_England_Ambulance_Service" title="East of England Ambulance Service">East of England Ambulance Service</a> is on Cambourne Business Park on <a href="/wiki/Cambourne" title="Cambourne">Cambourne</a>, off the <a href="/wiki/A428_road" title="A428 road">A428</a> (the former <a href="/wiki/A45_road" title="A45 road">A45</a>) west of Cambridge. The <a href="/wiki/East_Anglian_Air_Ambulance" title="East Anglian Air Ambulance">East Anglian Air Ambulance</a> operates from <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Airport" title="Cambridge Airport">Cambridge Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwich International Airport">Norwich Airport</a>; <a href="/wiki/Essex_Air_Ambulance" class="mw-redirect" title="Essex Air Ambulance">Essex Air Ambulance</a> operates from <a href="/wiki/Boreham" title="Boreham">Boreham</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hertfordshire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WetherspoonsPboro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/WetherspoonsPboro.jpg/220px-WetherspoonsPboro.jpg" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/WetherspoonsPboro.jpg/330px-WetherspoonsPboro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/WetherspoonsPboro.jpg/440px-WetherspoonsPboro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1397" data-file-height="1437" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WetherspoonsPboro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wetherspoons is based in Watford near <a href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_railway_station" title="Watford Junction railway station">Watford Junction railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Greater <a href="/wiki/Watford" title="Watford">Watford</a> area is home to <a href="/wiki/British_Waterways" title="British Waterways">British Waterways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinci_(construction)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinci (construction)">Vinci UK</a> (which bought <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Woodrow_Construction" class="mw-redirect" title="Taylor Woodrow Construction">Taylor Woodrow Construction</a> in 2008), the UK of the international firm <a href="/wiki/Total_Oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Total Oil">Total Oil</a>, retailers <a href="/wiki/TK_Maxx" title="TK Maxx">TK Maxx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bathstore" title="Bathstore">Bathstore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Majestic_Wine" title="Majestic Wine">Majestic Wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mothercare" title="Mothercare">Mothercare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costco" title="Costco">Costco UK</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Smiths_Group" title="Smiths Group">Smiths Detection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/BrightHouse_(retailer)" title="BrightHouse (retailer)">BrightHouse</a> (at <a href="/wiki/Abbots_Langley" title="Abbots Langley">Abbots Langley</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leavesden_Film_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Leavesden Film Studios">Leavesden Film Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanyo" title="Sanyo">Sanyo UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europcar" title="Europcar">Europcar UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympus_Corporation" title="Olympus Corporation">Olympus UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenwood_Corporation" title="Kenwood Corporation">Kenwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beko" title="Beko">Beko</a> electronic goods manufacturers, <a href="/wiki/Wetherspoons" title="Wetherspoons">Wetherspoons</a> pub chains, the European HQ of the <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Worldwide" title="Hilton Worldwide">Hilton</a> hotel group and <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestl\xc3\xa9">Nestl\xc3\xa9</a> Waters; in <a href="/wiki/Garston,_Hertfordshire" title="Garston, Hertfordshire">Garston</a> is the UK headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/A412_road" title="A412 road">A412</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Building_Research_Establishment" title="Building Research Establishment">Building Research Establishment</a>. <a href="/wiki/Comet_Group" title="Comet Group">Comet Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camelot_Group" title="Camelot Group">Camelot Group</a> (owners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Lottery_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Lottery (United Kingdom)">National Lottery</a>), on the <a href="/wiki/A4145_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A4145 road">A4145</a>, are in <a href="/wiki/Rickmansworth" title="Rickmansworth">Rickmansworth</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ferrero_SpA" title="Ferrero SpA">Ferrero UK</a> (maker of <a href="/wiki/Nutella" title="Nutella">Nutella</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kinder_Chocolate" title="Kinder Chocolate">Kinder Chocolate</a>) is in <a href="/wiki/Croxley_Green" title="Croxley Green">Croxley Green</a>. <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skanska" title="Skanska">Skanska UK</a> (construction) are in <a href="/wiki/Maple_Cross" title="Maple Cross">Maple Cross</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Elstree" title="Elstree">Elstree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borehamwood" title="Borehamwood">Borehamwood</a> (close to the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1 motorway</a>) are the <a href="/wiki/Elstree_Studios" title="Elstree Studios">Elstree Studios</a>, where the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> films were made and more recently <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Brother (TV series)">Big Brother</a></i>; and <a href="/wiki/Hasselblad" title="Hasselblad">Hasselblad UK</a> is based in Elstree. Borehamwood is also home to BBC Elstree and <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut UK</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boy%27s_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="Boy&#39;s Brigade">Boy\'s Brigade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dixons_Retail" title="Dixons Retail">Dixons Retail</a> (owners of <a href="/wiki/Currys" title="Currys">Currys</a>) and <a href="/wiki/PC_World_(retailer)" title="PC World (retailer)">PC World</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sir_Robert_McAlpine" title="Sir Robert McAlpine">Sir Robert McAlpine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Leisure" title="Bourne Leisure">Bourne Leisure</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Hemel_Hempstead" title="Hemel Hempstead">Hemel Hempstead</a>, where <a href="/wiki/3Com" title="3Com">3Com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seiko_Epson" title="Seiko Epson">Epson UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steria" class="mw-redirect" title="Steria">Steria</a> (formerly Bull and Honeywell), <a href="/wiki/Alcon" title="Alcon">Alcon UK</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kodak" title="Kodak">Kodak</a> have their UK bases. <a href="/wiki/Henkel" title="Henkel">Henkel</a> UK makes (<a href="/wiki/Loctite" title="Loctite">Loctite</a>) industrial <a href="/wiki/Adhesive" title="Adhesive">adhesives</a> off the A4147, next to Dixons. <a href="/wiki/Pure_Digital" class="mw-redirect" title="Pure Digital">Pure Digital</a> (DAB radios) is in <a href="/wiki/Kings_Langley" title="Kings Langley">Kings Langley</a>, with its parent company <a href="/wiki/Imagination_Technologies" title="Imagination Technologies">Imagination Technologies</a> which is a world-leading designer of microprocessors. The town was formerly the home of <a href="/wiki/Ovaltine" title="Ovaltine">Ovaltine</a> until 2002. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Noble_Foods&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Noble Foods (page does not exist)">Noble Foods</a> on the B488 in Tring is the UK\'s biggest producer of eggs.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg/300px-Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg" width="300" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg/450px-Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg/600px-Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a>\'s headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Hatfield,_Hertfordshire" title="Hatfield, Hertfordshire">Hatfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Welwyn_Garden_City" title="Welwyn Garden City">Welwyn Garden City</a> are <a href="/wiki/PayPoint" title="PayPoint">PayPoint</a>, the former headquarters of <a href="/wiki/First_Quench_Retailing" title="First Quench Retailing">First Quench Retailing</a> until 2009 (formerly the Thresher Group), <a href="/wiki/Hostelling_International" title="Hostelling International">Hostelling International</a>, the UK headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cereal_Partners_Worldwide" title="Cereal Partners Worldwide">Cereal Partners</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=DBC_Foodservice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="DBC Foodservice (page does not exist)">DBC Foodservice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hoffmann%E2%80%93La_Roche" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoffmann\xe2\x80\x93La Roche">Hoffmann\xe2\x80\x93La Roche</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Shredded_Wheat" class="mw-redirect" title="Shredded Wheat">Shredded Wheat</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shreddies" title="Shreddies">Shreddies</a></i> were manufactured in the town by <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestl\xc3\xa9">Nestl\xc3\xa9</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cereal_Partners_Worldwide" title="Cereal Partners Worldwide">Cereal Partners</a>) until April 2008, which has its UK headquarters at the A1000/B195 junction. <a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">DuPont UK</a> and a plant of GSK are in <a href="/wiki/Stevenage" title="Stevenage">Stevenage</a>. <a href="/wiki/EADS_Astrium" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS Astrium">EADS Astrium UK</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Paradigm_Secure_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Paradigm Secure Communications">Paradigm Secure Communications</a> (a <a href="/wiki/List_of_communication_satellite_companies" title="List of communication satellite companies">satellite operator</a>) (which has made parts for the <a href="/wiki/ExoMars" title="ExoMars">ExoMars</a> mission, <a href="/wiki/Gaia_(spacecraft)" title="Gaia (spacecraft)">Gaia (spacecraft)</a>, <a href="/wiki/ADM-Aeolus" title="ADM-Aeolus">ADM-Aeolus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LISA_Pathfinder" title="LISA Pathfinder">LISA Pathfinder</a>) and <a href="/wiki/MBDA" title="MBDA">MBDA UK</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Propellers" title="De Havilland Propellers">de Havilland Propellers</a>, then <a href="/wiki/BAe_Dynamics" title="BAe Dynamics">BAe Dynamics</a>) are near the A1(M) bypass opposite each other on the A1072. <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Crompton_Lighting&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crompton Lighting (page does not exist)">Crompton Lighting</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Cheshunt" title="Cheshunt">Cheshunt</a>. <a href="/wiki/Computacenter" title="Computacenter">Computacenter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denso" title="Denso">Denso UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/EE_(telecommunications_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="EE (telecommunications company)">EE</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Hatfield,_Hertfordshire" title="Hatfield, Hertfordshire">Hatfield</a>; <a href="/wiki/Veolia_Water_Central_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Veolia Water Central Limited">Veolia Water Central Limited</a> and the HQ of <a href="/wiki/Ocado" title="Ocado">Ocado</a> are next to each other on the A1001. <a href="/wiki/Polaroid_Corporation" title="Polaroid Corporation">Polaroid UK</a> (near the railway bridge over the A1081), <a href="/wiki/Burton%27s_Foods" class="mw-redirect" title="Burton&#39;s Foods">Burton\'s Biscuit Company</a> (on the B691) and <a href="/wiki/Premier_Foods" title="Premier Foods">Premier Foods</a> are in <a href="/wiki/St_Albans" title="St Albans">St Albans</a>; also <a href="/wiki/Murphy_Oil" title="Murphy Oil">Murphy Oil</a> Corp\'s USA, UK subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Murco_Petroleum_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Murco Petroleum Ltd">Murco Petroleum Ltd</a>; <a href="/wiki/The_Cloud_(company)" title="The Cloud (company)">The Cloud</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(Wi-Fi)" title="Hotspot (Wi-Fi)">wifi hotspots</a>, owned by BSkyB), is next to the <a href="/wiki/St_Albans_City_railway_station" title="St Albans City railway station">railway station</a>. <a href="/wiki/Viglen" title="Viglen">Viglen</a> is on the <a href="/wiki/A5183_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A5183 road">A5183</a> (the former A5) next to the M25 and <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">railway</a> at Ventura Park, the former site of <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page" title="Handley Page">Handley Page</a> at <a href="/wiki/Colney_Street" title="Colney Street">Colney Street</a> (<a href="/wiki/St_Stephen,_Hertfordshire" title="St Stephen, Hertfordshire">St Stephen</a>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Johnson_Matthey" title="Johnson Matthey">Johnson Matthey</a> (materials for <a href="/wiki/Catalytic_converter" title="Catalytic converter">catalytic converters</a>) has its main operations in <a href="/wiki/Royston,_Hertfordshire" title="Royston, Hertfordshire">Royston</a>. Royde &amp; Tucker in Hitchin, Hertfordshire is the UK\'s leading manufacturer of door <a href="/wiki/Hinge" title="Hinge">hinges</a>, and William Ransom &amp; Son makes pharmaceuticals and <a href="/wiki/Alternative_medicine" title="Alternative medicine">natural remedies</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cash_Converters" title="Cash Converters">Cash Converters UK</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Thundridge" title="Thundridge">Thundridge</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ware,_Hertfordshire" title="Ware, Hertfordshire">Ware</a>. <a href="/wiki/News_International" class="mw-redirect" title="News International">News International</a> has the world\'s largest printing press at <a href="/wiki/Broxbourne" title="Broxbourne">Broxbourne</a> (<a href="/wiki/Waltham_Cross" title="Waltham Cross">Waltham Cross</a>). <a href="/wiki/Harlow" title="Harlow">Harlow</a> has <a href="/wiki/Pearson_Education" title="Pearson Education">Pearson Education</a>, the main research division of <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a> (on a former BP site), the European headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Pitney_Bowes" title="Pitney Bowes">Pitney Bowes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synthomer" title="Synthomer">Synthomer</a> (polymers), and the main manufacturing plant of <a href="/wiki/Raytheon" title="Raytheon">Raytheon UK</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rexel" title="Rexel">Rexel UK</a> (electrical supplies) is based at the <a href="/wiki/A111_road_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="A111 road (England)">A111</a>/<a href="/wiki/A1000_road" title="A1000 road">A1000</a> junction in <a href="/wiki/Potters_Bar" title="Potters Bar">Potters Bar</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bedfordshire">Bedfordshire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bedfordshire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Samuel_whitbread_1720-1796_by_joshua_reynolds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Samuel_whitbread_1720-1796_by_joshua_reynolds.jpg/220px-Samuel_whitbread_1720-1796_by_joshua_reynolds.jpg"
