/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Samuel_whitbread_1720-1796_by_joshua_reynolds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Samuel_Whitbread_(1720%E2%80%931796)" title="Samuel Whitbread (1720\xe2\x80\x931796)">Samuel Whitbread</a> began his brewery in Bedfordshire in 1742</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Moto_Hospitality" title="Moto Hospitality">Moto Hospitality</a> has its headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Toddington,_Bedfordshire" title="Toddington, Bedfordshire">Toddington</a> in Bedfordshire (at the <a href="/wiki/Toddington_services" title="Toddington services">service station</a>).\n</p><p>Luton is home to <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a> (both based at the airport), <a href="/wiki/Hain_Celestial_Group" title="Hain Celestial Group">Hain Celestial Group UK</a> (which makes <a href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney_Foods" title="Linda McCartney Foods">Linda McCartney Foods</a>, and is based on the B579 in <a href="/wiki/Biscot" title="Biscot">Biscot</a>), <a href="/wiki/Eurolines" title="Eurolines">Eurolines</a> (UK office), <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Holidays" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson Holidays">Thomson UK</a> (based at <a href="/wiki/Wigmore,_Luton" title="Wigmore, Luton">Wigmore</a> on the eastern edge of the town), and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet UK</a> (at Griffin House, the Vauxhall head office). At the 85-acre <a href="/wiki/Capability_Green" class="mw-redirect" title="Capability Green">Capability Green</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A1081_road" title="A1081 road">A1081</a> and junction 10a of the M1, is the <a href="/wiki/Stonegate_Pub_Company" title="Stonegate Pub Company">Stonegate Pub Company</a> (owner of <a href="/wiki/Scream_Pubs" title="Scream Pubs">Scream Pubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yates%27s" title="Yates&#39;s">Yates\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slug_and_Lettuce_(pub_chain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Slug and Lettuce (pub chain)">Slug and Lettuce</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hogshead_(pub_chain)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hogshead (pub chain) (page does not exist)">Hogshead</a>), <a href="/wiki/InBev" title="InBev">InBev</a> UK (which bought most of Whitbread\'s beer brands), Chargemaster (<a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">electric vehicle network</a> under the POLAR brand), <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>\'s UK Marketing Company division, and <a href="/wiki/Alexon_Group" title="Alexon Group">Alexon Group</a> (ladies clothing). <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall" title="Vauxhall">Vauxhall</a> produced its last <a href="/wiki/Opel_Vectra" title="Opel Vectra">Vauxhall Vectra</a> in March 2002 at the plant near the A6/A505 roundabout, and now makes vans (<a href="/wiki/Opel_Vivaro_B" class="mw-redirect" title="Opel Vivaro B">Vivaro</a>/<a href="/wiki/Renault_Trafic" title="Renault Trafic">Renault Trafic</a>) at the former <a href="/wiki/Bedford_Vehicles" title="Bedford Vehicles">Bedford Vehicles</a> plant, based in the north of the town at the <a href="/wiki/GM_Manufacturing_Luton" class="mw-redirect" title="GM Manufacturing Luton">GM Manufacturing Luton</a> plant. Near <a href="/wiki/Luton_railway_station" title="Luton railway station">Luton railway station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comau" title="Comau">Comau Estil</a> is a manufacturing <a href="/wiki/Systems_integrator" title="Systems integrator">systems integrator</a> for car manufacturers. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Elster_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Elster Group (page does not exist)">Elster Metering</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Gas_meter" title="Gas meter">gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electricity_meter" title="Electricity meter">electricity meters</a>, and is based in the north of Luton on the opposite side of the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">railway</a> to Vauxhall. <a href="/w/index.php?title=GKN_Aerospace_Transparency_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GKN Aerospace Transparency Systems (page does not exist)">GKN Aerospace Transparency Systems</a> (formerly Pilkington Aerospace before 2003), the world\'s leading manufacturer of military <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_canopy" title="Aircraft canopy">aircraft canopies</a>, which also makes <a href="/wiki/Ice_protection_system" title="Ice protection system">ice protection systems</a>, is at <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">Luton Airport</a>. <a href="/wiki/ArjoHuntleigh" title="ArjoHuntleigh">ArjoHuntleigh</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/A505_road" title="A505 road">A505</a> in Luton near the M1, is a leading medical equipment manufacturer, and nearby, Certwood made the plastic seats for London\'s <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Stadium (London)">Olympic Stadium</a>. <a href="/wiki/Premier_Inn" title="Premier Inn">Premier Inn</a> (owned by Whitbread) is headquartered, with the UK headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Electrolux" title="Electrolux">Electrolux</a> (owner of <a href="/wiki/AEG" title="AEG">AEG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zanussi" title="Zanussi">Zanussi</a>), in <a href="/wiki/Leagrave" title="Leagrave">Leagrave</a>, north Luton. Its neighbour in <a href="/wiki/Dunstable" title="Dunstable">Dunstable</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Whitbread" title="Whitbread">Whitbread</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Polestar_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Polestar (company) (page does not exist)">Polestar</a>, a main magazine printers.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg/220px-Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg/330px-Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg/440px-Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wigmore_Place_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1372797.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wigmore House in Luton, home of TUI UK, and <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson Airways">Thomson Airways</a>, the world\'s largest charter airline</div></div></div>\n<p>Bedford is home to <a href="/wiki/Fujifilm" title="Fujifilm">Fujifilm UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wells_%26_Young%27s_Brewery" title="Wells &amp; Young&#39;s Brewery">Wells &amp; Young\'s Brewery</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Charles_Wells_Ltd" title="Charles Wells Ltd">Charles Wells</a>). <a href="/wiki/Danfoss" title="Danfoss">Danfoss Randall</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Thermostat" title="Thermostat">heating controls</a> on the A6 next to <a href="/wiki/Bedford_St_Johns_railway_station" title="Bedford St Johns railway station">Bedford St Johns railway station</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boxclever" title="Boxclever">boxclever</a> is south of the town on the A6. <a href="/wiki/Autoglass" class="mw-redirect" title="Autoglass">Autoglass</a> is in nearby <a href="/wiki/Cardington,_Bedfordshire" title="Cardington, Bedfordshire">Cardington</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunter_Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hunter Engineering (page does not exist)">Hunter Engineering</a> UK (defence) is at <a href="/wiki/Ampthill" title="Ampthill">Ampthill</a>. <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon UK</a> has its main distribution centre for England (its first in the UK, established in May 1999)<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> at the <a href="/wiki/ProLogis" class="mw-redirect" title="ProLogis">ProLogis</a> Marston Gate<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> site at <a href="/wiki/Brogborough" title="Brogborough">Brogborough</a> near junction 13 of the M1 (<a href="/wiki/A421_road" title="A421 road">A421</a>) next to <a href="/wiki/Ridgmont_railway_station" title="Ridgmont railway station">Ridgmont railway station</a>. Hanson Building Products was the largest producer of aggregates in the world, being taken over by <a href="/wiki/HeidelbergCement" title="HeidelbergCement">HeidelbergCement</a> in August 2007, and has always been based at Stewartby off the <a href="/wiki/A421_road" title="A421 road">A421</a> south of Bedford next to the <a href="/wiki/Stewartby_railway_station" title="Stewartby railway station">railway station</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kier_Group" title="Kier Group">Kier Group</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_for_the_Protection_of_Birds" title="Royal Society for the Protection of Birds">RSPB</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Sandy,_Bedfordshire" title="Sandy, Bedfordshire">Sandy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Connells" class="mw-redirect" title="Connells">Connells</a> and <a href="/wiki/UltraVision" title="UltraVision">UltraVision</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Leighton_Buzzard" title="Leighton Buzzard">Leighton Buzzard</a>. <a href="/wiki/Leisure_Connection" title="Leisure Connection">Leisure Connection</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Wyboston" title="Wyboston">Wyboston</a>, towards St Neots. <a href="/wiki/Jordans_(company)" title="Jordans (company)">Jordans</a> (cereal), <a href="/w/index.php?title=AMG_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="AMG Systems (page does not exist)">AMG Systems</a> (electronics) and <a href="/wiki/Liebherr_Group" title="Liebherr Group">Liebherr Group UK</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Biggleswade" title="Biggleswade">Biggleswade</a>. <a href="/wiki/Trafficmaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Trafficmaster">Trafficmaster</a> Europe and <a href="/wiki/Saab_Automobile" title="Saab Automobile">Saab Great Britain</a> are at <a href="/wiki/Cranfield_University" title="Cranfield University">Cranfield University</a>. <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a> has its main food research site (where low fat spreads were invented) at <a href="/wiki/Colworth_Science_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Colworth Science Park">Colworth Science Park</a> near <a href="/wiki/Sharnbrook" title="Sharnbrook">Sharnbrook</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Anglia">East Anglia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: East Anglia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg/220px-Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg.png" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg/330px-Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg/440px-Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_East_Anglia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of East Anglia</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg/220px-Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg/330px-Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg/440px-Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Witchingham_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73615.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Great_Witchingham_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Witchingham Hall">Great Witchingham Hall</a>, the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Matthews_Farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernard Matthews Farms">Bernard Matthews Farms</a>, north-west of Norwich at <a href="/wiki/Great_Witchingham" title="Great Witchingham">Great Witchingham</a> on the <a href="/wiki/A1067_road" title="A1067 road">A1067</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The economy in Norfolk, Cambridgeshire and Suffolk is traditionally mostly agricultural. Norfolk is the UK\'s biggest producer of potatoes. Nationally known companies include the <a href="/wiki/RAC_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="RAC plc">RAC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archant" title="Archant">Archant</a> (publishing), <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Money_UK" title="Virgin Money UK">Virgin Money</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aviva" title="Aviva">Aviva</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Norwich_Union" title="Norwich Union">Norwich Union</a>) in Norwich. In Carrow, to the east of the city, <a href="/wiki/Colman%27s" title="Colman&#39;s">Colman\'s</a> makes a wide range of mustards, and <a href="/wiki/Britvic" title="Britvic">Britvic</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Robinsons_(drink)" title="Robinsons (drink)">Robinsons</a> squash, which was owned by Colman\'s until 1995. Across the <a href="/wiki/River_Yare" title="River Yare">River Yare</a> near the A47/<a href="/wiki/A146_road" title="A146 road">A146</a> junction in <a href="/wiki/Trowse" title="Trowse">Trowse with Newton</a> is <a href="/wiki/May_Gurney" class="mw-redirect" title="May Gurney">May Gurney</a>, the construction company. <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Matthews_Farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernard Matthews Farms">Bernard Matthews Farms</a> has a large turkey farm on the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Attlebridge" title="RAF Attlebridge">RAF Attlebridge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Weston_Longville" title="Weston Longville">Weston Longville</a>. <a href="/wiki/Campbell_Soup_Company" title="Campbell Soup Company">Campbell Soup</a> was made in <a href="/wiki/Kings_Lynn" class="mw-redirect" title="Kings Lynn">Kings Lynn</a> until 2008, and on the Hardwick Industrial Estate at the A47/<a href="/wiki/A149_road" title="A149 road">A149</a> junction is <a href="/w/index.php?title=PinguinLutosa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="PinguinLutosa (page does not exist)">PinguinLutosa</a> UK, which packs <a href="/wiki/Frozen_vegetables" title="Frozen vegetables">frozen vegetables</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Caithness_Crystal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caithness Crystal (page does not exist)">Caithness Crystal</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Foster_Refrigerator&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Foster Refrigerator (page does not exist)">Foster Refrigerator</a> is the UK\'s leading manufacturer of commercial refrigerators and <a href="/wiki/Blast_chilling" title="Blast chilling">blast chillers</a>, owned by <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Tool_Works" title="Illinois Tool Works">Illinois Tool Works</a>, based on the industrial estate; with <a href="/wiki/Multitone_Electronics" title="Multitone Electronics">Multitone Electronics</a>, which has a manufacturing plant there, and which invented the <a href="/wiki/Pager" title="Pager">pager</a> in 1956, for <a href="/wiki/St_Thomas%27_Hospital" title="St Thomas&#39; Hospital">St Thomas\' Hospital</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Snap-on" title="Snap-on">Snap-on Diagnostics</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Machine_fault_diagnosis" class="mw-redirect" title="Machine fault diagnosis">diagnostic tools</a> for garages. Linda McCartney sausages are made by Hain Celestial Frozen Foods at <a href="/wiki/Fakenham" title="Fakenham">Fakenham</a>, where <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinnerton_Confectionery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kinnerton Confectionery (page does not exist)">Kinnerton Confectionery</a> produces around 6000 tonnes of chocolate each year, which is mostly private label (supermarket) products. British Sugar\'s <a href="/wiki/Wissington,_Norfolk" title="Wissington, Norfolk">Wissington</a> is the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beet</a> factory in <a href="/wiki/Methwold" title="Methwold">Methwold</a>, on the B1160 near the <a href="/wiki/River_Wissey" title="River Wissey">River Wissey</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Cars" title="Lotus Cars">Lotus Cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Team Lotus</a> are on the eastern edge of the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Hethel" title="RAF Hethel">RAF Hethel</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Wymondham" title="Wymondham">Wymondham</a> (A11) at <a href="/wiki/Hethel" title="Hethel">Hethel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bracon_Ash" title="Bracon Ash">Bracon Ash</a>). <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jeyes_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jeyes Group (page does not exist)">Jeyes Group</a> makes household chemicals in <a href="/wiki/Thetford" title="Thetford">Thetford</a>, off the <a href="/wiki/A134_road" title="A134 road">A134</a>; <a href="/wiki/Multiyork" title="Multiyork">Multiyork</a> makes furniture and <a href="/wiki/Baxter_International" title="Baxter International">Baxter Healthcare</a> has a manufacturing plant in the south of the town. <a href="/wiki/Aunt_Bessie" class="mw-redirect" title="Aunt Bessie">Aunt Bessie</a> vegetable products (roast potatoes) are made by <a href="/wiki/H._J._Heinz_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="H. J. Heinz Company">Heinz UK</a> at <a href="/wiki/Westwick,_Norfolk" title="Westwick, Norfolk">Westwick</a>, in a factory built by <a href="/wiki/Ross_Group" title="Ross Group">Ross Group</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:P60ARM_GC_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/P60ARM_GC_01.jpg/220px-P60ARM_GC_01.jpg" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/P60ARM_GC_01.jpg/330px-P60ARM_GC_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/P60ARM_GC_01.jpg/440px-P60ARM_GC_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="524" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:P60ARM_GC_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM CPU</a> designed in Cambridge</div></div></div>\n<p>Around Cambridge on numerous <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">science parks</a>, are high technology (electronics and biochemistry) companies, such as <a href="/wiki/ARM_Holdings" class="mw-redirect" title="ARM Holdings">ARM Holdings</a> on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peterhouse_Technology_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peterhouse Technology Park (page does not exist)">Peterhouse Technology Park</a> in the south-east of the town, <a href="/wiki/Adder_Technology" title="Adder Technology">Adder Technology</a> (<a href="/wiki/KVM_switch" title="KVM switch">KVM switches</a>) at <a href="/wiki/Bar_Hill" title="Bar Hill">Bar Hill</a> at the <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14</a>/B1050 junction north of the town, <a href="/wiki/Monsanto" title="Monsanto">Monsanto UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Play.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Play.com">Play.com</a> on the Cambridge Business Centre. The <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust_Genome_Campus" class="mw-redirect" title="Wellcome Trust Genome Campus">Wellcome Trust Genome Campus</a> has the <a href="/wiki/European_Bioinformatics_Institute" title="European Bioinformatics Institute">European Bioinformatics Institute</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hinxton" title="Hinxton">Hinxton</a> east of Duxford near the M11 spur for the A11. These form the so-called <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Fen" title="Silicon Fen">Silicon Fen</a>. <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall Aerospace">Marshall Aerospace</a> is at <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Airport" title="Cambridge Airport">Cambridge Airport</a> on the <a href="/wiki/A1303_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A1303 road">A1303</a> in the east of the town, towards <a href="/wiki/Teversham" title="Teversham">Teversham</a>. South of the airport, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Zeiss_AG" title="Carl Zeiss AG">Carl Zeiss NTS</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Scanning_electron_microscope" title="Scanning electron microscope">scanning electron microscopes</a> in Cherry Hinton. <a href="/wiki/Syngenta" title="Syngenta">Syngenta UK</a> is to the east of Cambridge, on Capital Park at <a href="/wiki/Fulbourn" title="Fulbourn">Fulbourn</a>. <a href="/wiki/Premier_Foods" title="Premier Foods">Premier Foods</a> has a large plant in <a href="/wiki/Histon_and_Impington" title="Histon and Impington">Histon and Impington</a> making <a href="/wiki/Robertson%27s" title="Robertson&#39;s">Robertson\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hartley%27s" title="Hartley&#39;s">Hartley\'s</a> jam, <a href="/wiki/Gale%27s" title="Gale&#39;s">Gale\'s</a> honey, <a href="/wiki/Smash_(instant_mashed_potato)" title="Smash (instant mashed potato)">Smash</a> <a href="/wiki/Instant_mashed_potatoes" title="Instant mashed potatoes">instant potato</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rose%27s_(marmalade)" title="Rose&#39;s (marmalade)">Rose\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Marmalade" title="Marmalade">marmalade</a>. <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke\'s Hospital</a> is a pioneering hospital in the UK, based at <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Bio-Medical_Campus" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Bio-Medical Campus">Cambridge Bio-Medical Campus</a>. On the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Science_Park" title="Cambridge Science Park">Cambridge Science Park</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Cambridgeshire" title="Milton, Cambridgeshire">Milton</a>), the first science park in Europe (when founded in 1970 by <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Cambridge" title="Trinity College, Cambridge">Trinity College</a>), near the junction of the A14 and A10 (<a href="/wiki/A1309_road" title="A1309 road">A1309</a>) and on the western side of the A1309 in <a href="/wiki/South_Cambridgeshire" title="South Cambridgeshire">South Cambridgeshire</a>, are <a href="/wiki/WorldPay" class="mw-redirect" title="WorldPay">WorldPay</a> (<a href="/wiki/Payment_service_provider" title="Payment service provider">payment service provider</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jagex" title="Jagex">Jagex</a> (<a href="/wiki/RuneScape" title="RuneScape">RuneScape</a>), the European HQ of <a href="/wiki/Accelrys" title="Accelrys">Accelrys</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge_Consultants&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cambridge Consultants (page does not exist)">Cambridge Consultants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astex" title="Astex">Astex</a> (biotechnology), <a href="/wiki/Eastman_Kodak" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastman Kodak">Kodak</a>\'s European R&amp;D centre, and <a href="/wiki/Broadcom" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadcom">Broadcom UK</a>. On <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Business_Park" title="Cambridge Business Park">Cambridge Business Park</a>, on the eastern side of the A1309 (formerly the A10) and inside the district of Cambridge, are <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomy Corporation">Autonomy Corporation</a>, an FTSE-100 company, <a href="/wiki/Red_Gate_Software" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Gate Software">Red Gate Software</a>, <a href="/wiki/CSR_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="CSR plc">CSR plc</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NEC_Unified_Solutions" title="NEC Unified Solutions">NEC Unified Solutions UK</a> (<a href="/wiki/Unified_communications" title="Unified communications">unified communications</a>). On the 200-acre <a href="/wiki/Granta_Park" title="Granta Park">Granta Park</a> at <a href="/wiki/Great_Abington" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Abington">Great Abington</a> near the A1307/A11 junction south of Cambridge is <a href="/wiki/MedImmune" title="MedImmune">MedImmune</a> (formerly Cambridge Antibody Technology, now owned by <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>) which researches antibodies. <a href="/wiki/The_Welding_Institute" title="The Welding Institute">The Welding Institute</a>, Pfizer Regenerative Medicine, <a href="/wiki/Gilead_Sciences" title="Gilead Sciences">Gilead Sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_Product_Development" title="Pharmaceutical Product Development">PPD</a> are nearby. The science park has its own cricket pitch.\n</p><p>Cambridgeshire has a few <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> bases. <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway UK</a> (restaurants) is in <a href="/wiki/Great_Shelford" title="Great Shelford">Great Shelford</a>. <a href="/wiki/Unwins_Seeds" title="Unwins Seeds">Unwins Seeds</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Alconbury_Weston" title="Alconbury Weston">Alconbury Weston</a> next to the A1. Avanquest UK, the home software company which bought EMME (which bought GSP in 2000) in 2007, is in <a href="/wiki/St_Ives,_Cambridgeshire" title="St Ives, Cambridgeshire">St Ives</a>, off the A1096. <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9_Purina_PetCare" title="Nestl\xc3\xa9 Purina PetCare">Nestl\xc3\xa9 Purina PetCare</a> makes petfood at its South Brink factory in <a href="/wiki/Wisbech" title="Wisbech">Wisbech</a>, with another in <a href="/wiki/Sudbury,_Suffolk" title="Sudbury, Suffolk">Sudbury, Suffolk</a>. <a href="/wiki/Princes_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Princes (company)">Princes</a> (formerly owned by <a href="/wiki/Premier_Foods" title="Premier Foods">Premier Foods</a> before February 2011) can vegetables and baked beans, and makes <a href="/wiki/Loyd_Grossman" title="Loyd Grossman">Loyd Grossman</a> cooking sauces in the town. <a href="/wiki/ConAgra_Foods" class="mw-redirect" title="ConAgra Foods">Lamb Weston</a> (potato products) is on the Weasanham Lane Ind Estate in the south of Wisbech, and next door <a href="/wiki/Fresh_Del_Monte_Produce" title="Fresh Del Monte Produce">Del Monte</a> can fruit. On the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Level_Navigations" title="Middle Level Navigations">Middle Level Main Drain</a> at <a href="/wiki/Marshland_St_James" title="Marshland St James">Marshland St James</a>, south of Wisbech, Herbert Engineering is Britain\'s main producer of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Potato_grader&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Potato grader (page does not exist)">potato graders</a>. The main water company for the area, <a href="/wiki/AWG_plc" title="AWG plc">AWG plc</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Audio_Group" title="International Audio Group">International Audio Group</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon" title="Huntingdon">Huntingdon</a>. JDR Cable Systems makes <a href="/wiki/Submarine_power_cable" title="Submarine power cable">underwater cables</a> at the <a href="/wiki/A10_road_(England)" title="A10 road (England)">A10</a>/A1101 roundabout at <a href="/wiki/Littleport,_Cambridgeshire" title="Littleport, Cambridgeshire">Littleport</a>. <a href="/wiki/McCain_Foods" title="McCain Foods">McCain Foods</a> has a factory (which was the largest frozen food factory in the world when it opened in 1976, processing 200,000 tonnes of potatoes annually) on the <a href="/wiki/A605_road" title="A605 road">A605</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ely_to_Peterborough_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Ely to Peterborough Line">railway</a>, near London Brick, at Whittlesey, towards Peterborough.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Thomas_Cook_Business_Park,_Peterborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_129412.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Thomas_Cook_Business_Park,_Peterborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_129412.jpg" Peterborough</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/RAF_Wittering" title="RAF Wittering">RAF Wittering</a> was the home of the <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_Harrier_II" title="British Aerospace Harrier II">Harrier</a> from August 1969 until December 2010, and now houses Army personnel, along with the RAF Regiment. <a href="/wiki/British_Sugar_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="British Sugar plc">British Sugar</a>, Silver Spoon and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Billington_Food_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Billington Food Group (page does not exist)">Billington Food Group</a> are based near each other in Peterborough, as is <a href="/wiki/Perkins_Engines_Company_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Perkins Engines Company Limited">Perkins Engines</a> (<a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a>). <a href="/wiki/News_International" class="mw-redirect" title="News International">News International</a> has a main office there and <a href="/wiki/Indesit" class="mw-redirect" title="Indesit">Indesit</a> (owner of <a href="/wiki/Hotpoint" title="Hotpoint">Hotpoint</a>, previously owned by <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Company_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="General Electric Company plc">GEC</a> before 2007) has its UK headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Woodston,_Peterborough" title="Woodston, Peterborough">Woodston</a>. Next door is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Applied_Energy_Products&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Applied Energy Products (page does not exist)">Applied Energy Products</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Glen_Dimplex" class="mw-redirect" title="Glen Dimplex">Glen Dimplex</a>), which owns <a href="/wiki/Redring" class="mw-redirect" title="Redring">Redring</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Credair&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Credair (page does not exist)">Credair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xpelair" class="mw-redirect" title="Xpelair">Xpelair</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Norwich_and_Peterborough_Building_Society" title="Norwich and Peterborough Building Society">N&amp;P Building Society</a> (since November 2011 part of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Building_Society" title="Yorkshire Building Society">Yorkshire Building Society</a>) is in <a href="/wiki/Orton_Waterville" class="mw-redirect" title="Orton Waterville">Orton Northgate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bauer_Radio" title="Bauer Radio">Bauer Radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bauer_Media_Group" title="Bauer Media Group">Bauer Consumer Media</a> (formerly EMAP Consumer Media) are headquartered on <i>Lincoln Road</i>. <a href="/wiki/EMAP" class="mw-redirect" title="EMAP">EMAP</a> has its magazine headquarters off the A605 in Orton Wistow; and <a href="/wiki/BGL_Group" title="BGL Group">BGL Group</a> (<i>Compare The Market</i>) is in <a href="/wiki/Orton,_Peterborough" title="Orton, Peterborough">Orton Southgate</a> next to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peterborough_services&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peterborough services (page does not exist)">Peterborough services</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ronart_Cars" title="Ronart Cars">Ronart Cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radical_Sportscars" title="Radical Sportscars">Radical Sportscars</a> develop sports cars at <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Peterborough" title="Westwood, Peterborough">Westwood</a>. <a href="/wiki/Baker_Perkins" title="Baker Perkins">Baker Perkins</a> makes food processing equipment next to the <i>Paston Parkway</i> (A15) in <a href="/wiki/Gunthorpe,_Peterborough" title="Gunthorpe, Peterborough">Gunthorpe</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG/220px-F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG/330px-F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG/440px-F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="2820" data-file-height="1860" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:F-100_Gate_Guard_RAF_Lakenheath.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gate guard at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Lakenheath" title="RAF Lakenheath">RAF Lakenheath</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> still has bases in Suffolk. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnsons_(seeds)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Johnsons (seeds) (page does not exist)">Johnsons</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mr_Fothergill%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mr Fothergill&#39;s (page does not exist)">Mr Fothergill\'s</a> produce seeds in <a href="/wiki/Kentford" title="Kentford">Kentford</a>, off the A14. In <a href="/wiki/Newmarket,_Suffolk" title="Newmarket, Suffolk">Newmarket</a> is the base of the <a href="/wiki/Horseracing_in_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Horseracing in Great Britain">British horse racing industry</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Horseracing_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="National Horseracing Museum">National Horseracing Museum</a>. <a href="/wiki/CLAAS" class="mw-redirect" title="CLAAS">CLAAS UK</a>, is based on the side of the A14 just west of Bury St Edmunds at <a href="/wiki/The_Saxhams" title="The Saxhams">The Saxhams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zetor" title="Zetor">Zetor Tractors</a> UK is in <a href="/wiki/Downham_Market" title="Downham Market">Downham Market</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_Ag" class="mw-redirect" title="New Holland Ag">New Holland UK</a> (and also the UK base of <a href="/wiki/Fiat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat">Fiat</a>-owned <a href="/wiki/CNH_Global" title="CNH Global">CNH Global</a>) is in <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a> where there is a large <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractor</a> factory. The <a href="/wiki/RAF_Regiment" title="RAF Regiment">RAF Regiment</a> is based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Honington" title="RAF Honington">RAF Honington</a>, between the A1088 and A134, south of Thetford, partly in <a href="/wiki/Fakenham_Magna" title="Fakenham Magna">Fakenham Magna</a>. The <a href="/wiki/100th_Air_Refueling_Wing" title="100th Air Refueling Wing">100th Air Refueling Wing</a>, which flies the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_KC-135_Stratotanker" title="Boeing KC-135 Stratotanker">KC-135</a> is at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Mildenhall" title="RAF Mildenhall">RAF Mildenhall</a>. Silverline is a main maker of steel office furniture (<a href="/wiki/Filing_cabinet" title="Filing cabinet">filing cabinets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tambour_desk" title="Tambour desk">tambour desks</a>) in Mildenhall, next to the airfield. <a href="/wiki/Greene_King" title="Greene King">Greene King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Branston_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Branston (food)">Branston Pickle</a> are in Bury St Edmunds, and British Sugar makes all its <a href="/wiki/Powdered_sugar" title="Powdered sugar">icing sugar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caster_sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="Caster sugar">caster sugar</a> there. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Helmsman_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Helmsman (company) (page does not exist)">Helmsman</a> is the UK\'s leading manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Changing_room" title="Changing room">changing room</a> cubicles and <a href="/wiki/Locker_(cabinet)" class="mw-redirect" title="Locker (cabinet)">lockers</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/A1101_road" title="A1101 road">A1101</a> at <a href="/wiki/Fornham_All_Saints" title="Fornham All Saints">Fornham All Saints</a>, north of Bury St Edmunds. <a href="/wiki/Vinten" title="Vinten">Vinten</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Camera_shoulder_support" class="mw-redirect" title="Camera shoulder support">camera supports</a> next to the A14, and is part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vitec_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vitec Group (page does not exist)">Vitec Group</a>. <a href="/wiki/BT_Research" title="BT Research">BT Research</a> has had its main labs at <a href="/wiki/Adastral_Park" title="Adastral Park">Adastral Park</a> near <a href="/wiki/Martlesham_Heath" title="Martlesham Heath">Martlesham Heath</a>, off the <a href="/wiki/A12_road_(England)" title="A12 road (England)">A12</a>, since 1975. This site now claims to be the largest software development centre in Europe. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Essfoods&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Essfoods (page does not exist)">Essfoods</a> is based at <a href="/wiki/Rendlesham_Hall" title="Rendlesham Hall">Rendlesham Hall</a> off the A1152, near the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Bentwaters" title="RAF Bentwaters">RAF Bentwaters</a>. <a href="/wiki/BOCM_Pauls" title="BOCM Pauls">BOCM Pauls</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Wherstead" title="Wherstead">Wherstead</a> just south of Ipswich. Ransomes Jacobsen (part of Textron) makes sit-down lawn mowers on the Ransomes Europark near the A14/A1189 junction. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Felixstowe" title="Port of Felixstowe">Port of Felixstowe</a> is the UK\'s busiest <a href="/wiki/Containerization" title="Containerization">container</a> terminal and the 28th <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports" title="List of busiest container ports">busiest</a> in the world. <a href="/wiki/Birds_Eye" title="Birds Eye">Birds Eye</a>, now no longer part of <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>, now has its main factories in <a href="/wiki/Lowestoft" title="Lowestoft">Lowestoft</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ness_Point" title="Ness Point">Ness Point</a>, and LEC Marine makes <a href="/wiki/Electric_switchboard" title="Electric switchboard">switchboards</a>. <a href="/wiki/SLP_Engineering" title="SLP Engineering">SLP Engineering</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">gas platforms</a> for the North Sea. <a href="/wiki/Adnams_Brewery" title="Adnams Brewery">Adnams Brewery</a> is on the Suffolk coast at <a href="/wiki/Southwold" title="Southwold">Southwold</a>. The electricity supplier Haven Power is based in Ipswich. <a href="/wiki/Thompson_and_Morgan" title="Thompson and Morgan">Thompson and Morgan</a> produces seeds, west of Ipswich just off the A14 at <a href="/wiki/Sproughton" title="Sproughton">Sproughton</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Becker_Acroma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Becker Acroma (page does not exist)">Becker Acroma</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Sherwin-Williams" title="Sherwin-Williams">Sherwin-Williams</a>) makes <a href="/wiki/Wood_finishing" title="Wood finishing">wood finishes</a> off the A1017 in <a href="/wiki/Haverhill,_Suffolk" title="Haverhill, Suffolk">Haverhill</a>, and on the same industrial estate <a href="/wiki/International_Flavors_%26_Fragrances" title="International Flavors &amp; Fragrances">International Flavors &amp; Fragrances</a> makes fragrances, and Marchant Manufacturing makes polythene (retail) bags.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Essex.2FGreater_London"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Essex/Greater_London">Essex/Greater London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Essex/Greater London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ford of Europe\'s Dunton Technical Centre</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/The_Scout_Association" title="The Scout Association">The Scout Association</a> is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Gilwell_Park" title="Gilwell Park">Gilwell Park</a> in south <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>. <a href="/wiki/Konica_Minolta" title="Konica Minolta">Konica Minolta Business Solutions (UK)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muddy_Fox" title="Muddy Fox">Muddy Fox</a> (mountain bikes) and <a href="/wiki/SELEX_Galileo" class="mw-redirect" title="SELEX Galileo">SELEX Galileo</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Avionics" title="BAE Systems Avionics">BAE Systems Avionics</a>) are in <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MK_Electric" title="MK Electric">MK Electric</a> makes circuit protection systems, and is based at Cranes near the <a href="/wiki/A127_road" title="A127 road">A127</a>/<a href="/wiki/A132_road_(England)" title="A132 road (England)">A132</a> junction, with a factory at Southend. <a href="/wiki/Britvic" title="Britvic">Britvic</a> is on the A1016 in <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford</a>, which is the historic home of the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Company" title="Marconi Company">Marconi Company</a> now run by <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a> at <a href="/wiki/Great_Baddow" title="Great Baddow">Great Baddow</a>. <a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">Federal Express Europe Inc</a> is at <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarke_International&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Clarke International (page does not exist)">Clarke International</a>, which makes electrical power equipment and tools, is on the B1393 (formerly the A11) in <a href="/wiki/Epping,_Essex" title="Epping, Essex">Epping</a>. <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinton Cards">Clinton Cards</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Loughton" title="Loughton">Loughton</a>, where <a href="/wiki/De_La_Rue" title="De La Rue">De La Rue</a> has a <a href="/wiki/Banknote" title="Banknote">banknote</a> <a href="/wiki/Security_printing" title="Security printing">printing</a> factory next to junction 5 of the M11, printing notes for the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England_note_issues" title="Bank of England note issues">Bank of England</a> and other countries. <a href="/wiki/Countrywide_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Countrywide plc">Countrywide plc</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Witham" title="Witham">Witham</a>, Essex.\n</p><p>The army has a large base in <a href="/wiki/Colchester_Garrison" title="Colchester Garrison">Colchester</a>, which is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Parachute_Regiment_(United_Kingdom)" title="Parachute Regiment (United Kingdom)">Parachute Regiment</a> and <a href="/wiki/16_Air_Assault_Brigade" title="16 Air Assault Brigade">16 Air Assault Brigade</a>. In the east of Colchester, off the <a href="/wiki/A134_road" title="A134 road">A134</a> is <a href="/wiki/MAN_Diesel_%26_Turbo" class="mw-redirect" title="MAN Diesel &amp; Turbo">MAN Diesel &amp; Turbo UK</a>, formerly owned by <a href="/wiki/Paxman_(engines)" title="Paxman (engines)">Paxmans</a>, which built the diesel engines for most UK trains, and further south in the town at <a href="/wiki/Hythe,_Essex" class="mw-redirect" title="Hythe, Essex">Hythe</a> there is <a href="/wiki/Chandos_Records" title="Chandos Records">Chandos Records</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_East_Anglia" title="Transport in East Anglia">Transport in East Anglia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_policy">Transport policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG/220px-Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG/330px-Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG/440px-Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Motorway_M11_Cambridge.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M11 near Cambridge</div></div></div>\n<p>As part of the transport planning system the Regional Assembly is under statutory requirement to produce a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Regional_Transport_Strategy_(UK)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Regional Transport Strategy (UK) (page does not exist)">Regional Transport Strategy (RTS)</a> to provide long term planning for transport in the region. This involves region wide transport schemes such as those carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Highways_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Highways Agency">Highways Agency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GoE1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoE1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Within the region the local transport authorities carry out transport planning through the use of a <a href="/wiki/Local_transport_plan" title="Local transport plan">Local Transport Plan (LTP)</a> which outlines their strategies, policies and implementation programme.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The most recent LTP is that for the period 2006-11. In the East of England region the following transport authorities have published their LTP online:\n<a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire" title="Bedfordshire">Bedfordshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BLTP_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BLTP-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire" title="Cambridgeshire">Cambridgeshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CLTP_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CLTP-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ELTP_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ELTP-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HLTP_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLTP-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a> U.A.,<sup id="cite_ref-LuLTP_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LuLTP-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NLTP_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLTP-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a> U.A.,<sup id="cite_ref-PLTP_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PLTP-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> U.A.,<sup id="cite_ref-SoSLTP_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SoSLTP-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Suffolk" title="Suffolk">Suffolk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SLTP_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SLTP-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Thurrock" title="Thurrock">Thurrock</a> U.A.<sup id="cite_ref-ThLTP_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThLTP-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Since 1 April 2009, when the county of Bedfordshire was split into two unitary councils,<sup id="cite_ref-Bed1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bed1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> the Bedfordshire transport authority has ceased to exist, however it is the most recent LTP for the area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orwell-Bridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Orwell-Bridge.jpg/220px-Orwell-Bridge.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Orwell-Bridge.jpg/330px-Orwell-Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Orwell-Bridge.jpg/440px-Orwell-Bridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orwell-Bridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Orwell_Bridge" title="Orwell Bridge">Orwell Bridge</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The East of England region is covered by the Highways Agency <a href="/wiki/Highways_Agency#Operational_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Highways Agency">operational area</a> 6 and part of area 8.\nMajor roads servicing these areas include the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a> London to Milton Keynes, <a href="/wiki/M11_motorway" title="M11 motorway">M11</a> London to Cambridge, <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">M25</a> through Hertfordshire and Essex, <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1</a> London to Peterborough, <a href="/wiki/A5_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A5 road (Great Britain)">A5</a> St. Albans to Milton Keynes, <a href="/wiki/A11_road_(England)" title="A11 road (England)">A11</a> London to Norwich, <a href="/wiki/A12_road_(England)" title="A12 road (England)">A12</a> London to Great Yarmouth, <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14</a> Felixstowe to Rugby via Cambridge, <a href="/wiki/A47_road" title="A47 road">A47</a> Great Yarmouth to Nuneaton and the <a href="/wiki/A120_road" title="A120 road">A120</a> Harwich to Stansted. There are a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_future_transport_developments_in_the_East_of_England#Road" title="List of future transport developments in the East of England">proposed road developments</a> throughout the region. Britain\'s first main motorway, the M1, opened at Toddington on 2 November 1959.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Milton_Ernest" title="Milton Ernest">Milton Ernest</a> in Bedfordshire, on the A6 north of Bedford, was the first UK place in December 2012 to have the Siemens <a href="/wiki/SafeZone" class="mw-redirect" title="SafeZone">SafeZone</a> average speed cameras (similar to <a href="/wiki/SPECS_(speed_camera)" title="SPECS (speed camera)">SPECS</a>, with much-reduced infrastructure) using <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sicore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sicore (page does not exist)">Sicore</a> <a href="/wiki/Automatic_number_plate_recognition" class="mw-redirect" title="Automatic number plate recognition">ANPR</a> cameras.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The region is serviced by Network Rail <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail_Route_5_(West_Anglia)" title="Network Rail Route 5 (West Anglia)">Route 5 West Anglia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail_Route_7_(Great_Eastern)" title="Network Rail Route 7 (Great Eastern)">Route 7 Great Eastern</a> as well as parts of\n<a href="/wiki/Network_Rail_Route_6_(North_London_Line_and_Thameside)" title="Network Rail Route 6 (North London Line and Thameside)">Route 6 North London Line and Thameside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail_Route_8_(East_Coast_Main_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Network Rail Route 8 (East Coast Main Line)">Route 8 East Coast Main Line</a>\nand <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail_Route_18_(West_Coast_Main_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Network Rail Route 18 (West Coast Main Line)">Route 18 West Coast Main Line</a>. Major rail lines run London to Norwich, London to Cambridge and <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn" title="King&#39;s Lynn">King\'s Lynn</a>, and London to Southend with a number of rural branch lines servicing the wider region. A major freight route also runs between the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Felixstowe" title="Port of Felixstowe">Port of Felixstowe</a> and London.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Colchester_railway_station" title="Colchester railway station">Colchester railway station</a> has the longest railway platform in the UK - around 620 metres, with <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_railway_station" title="Gloucester railway station">Gloucester railway station</a> second at 600m. The <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Coast_Line" title="Sunshine Coast Line">Sunshine Coast Line</a> was the first to be electrified in the country with <a href="/wiki/25_kV_AC_railway_electrification" title="25 kV AC railway electrification">25kV AC</a> overhead wires, with the first service from Colchester to <a href="/wiki/Great_Bentley_railway_station" title="Great Bentley railway station">Great Bentley</a> in April 1959.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Shippea_Hill_railway_station" title="Shippea Hill railway station">Shippea Hill railway station</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Breckland_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Breckland Line">Breckland Line</a> east of Ely at the crossing of the <a href="/wiki/A1101_road" title="A1101 road">A1101</a>, is the quietest railway station (by passengers) in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Buckenham_railway_station" title="Buckenham railway station">Buckenham railway station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Wherry_Lines" title="Wherry Lines">Wherry Lines</a> east of Norwich on the Norfolk Broads is the 9th quietest railway station in the UK.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg/220px-Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg/330px-Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg/440px-Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Humber_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1584615.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Felixstowe</div></div></div>\n<p>The East of England has one international <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> port, <a href="/wiki/Harwich_International_Port" title="Harwich International Port">Harwich International Port</a>, which together with the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Felixstowe" title="Port of Felixstowe">Port of Felixstowe</a>, the UK\'s largest container port, and the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ipswich#Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Ipswich">Port of Ipswich</a> forms the <a href="/wiki/Haven_ports" title="Haven ports">Haven ports</a> group.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/London_Gateway" title="London Gateway">London Gateway</a> container port on the Essex side of the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Estuary" title="Thames Estuary">Thames Estuary</a> was developed on the old <a href="/wiki/Shell_Haven" title="Shell Haven">Shell Haven</a> site and will have, when fully complete, 6 deep-water berths capable of docking the next generation of ultra large container ships.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tilbury" title="Port of Tilbury">Port of Tilbury</a> is also located on the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Estuary" title="Thames Estuary">Thames Estuary</a>, to the west of London Gateway.\n</p><p>The East of England coast also holds a number of traditional fishing ports including the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn_Docks" title="King&#39;s Lynn Docks">King\'s Lynn Docks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Lowestoft" title="Port of Lowestoft">Port of Lowestoft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Harbour" title="Wells Harbour">Wells Harbour</a>.\n<a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth_Outer_Harbour" title="Great Yarmouth Outer Harbour">Great Yarmouth Outer Harbour</a> opened in 2010 and along with the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Lowestoft" title="Port of Lowestoft">Port of Lowestoft</a> provides support for the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> energy industry, including the growing off-shore wind energy sector.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_STN.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/London_STN.JPG/220px-London_STN.JPG" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/London_STN.JPG/330px-London_STN.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/London_STN.JPG/440px-London_STN.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="876" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_STN.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stansted is <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>\'s biggest hub with <a href="/wiki/Ryanair_destinations" class="mw-redirect" title="Ryanair destinations">108 routes</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The region has four public international airports, <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Southend_Airport" title="London Southend Airport">London Southend Airport</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/RAF_Rochford" class="mw-redirect" title="RAF Rochford">RAF Rochford</a>), <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London Stansted Airport</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/RAF_Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="RAF Stansted Mountfitchet">RAF Stansted Mountfitchet</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwich International Airport">Norwich International Airport</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/RAF_Horsham_St_Faith" title="RAF Horsham St Faith">RAF Horsham St Faith</a>).\nIt also includes a number of smaller local airfields that are licensed for the public transport of passengers or for flying instruction; these include <a href="/wiki/Beccles_Airport" title="Beccles Airport">Beccles Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Airport" title="Cambridge Airport">Cambridge Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clacton_Airport" title="Clacton Airport">Clacton Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duxford_Aerodrome" title="Duxford Aerodrome">Duxford Aerodrome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peterborough/Sibson_Airport" title="Peterborough/Sibson Airport">Peterborough/Sibson Airport</a>.\n</p><p>Luton Airport is the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/EasyJet_destinations" class="mw-redirect" title="EasyJet destinations">easyjet</a>. With Luton and Stansted, the region has two of the best, if not the biggest, airline hubs in Europe. Stansted Airport, built in 1991, is the fourth busiest in the UK, with 17m passengers in 2012, and Luton is the fifth busiest with 9m. Stansted has not had any success in attracting long-haul flight routes.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg/220px-Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg/330px-Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg/440px-Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clare_College_Bridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_615505.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Clare_College_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Clare College Bridge">Clare College Bridge</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are around 255,000 at the region\'s secondary schools. Essex and Southend-on-Sea <a href="/wiki/Local_Education_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Education Authority">LEAs</a> have selective schools. In general, the region performs well at GCSE. The region overall has a low <a href="/wiki/Truancy" title="Truancy">truancy</a> rate. Within the region, <a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Yarmouth (borough)">Great Yarmouth</a> has the highest truancy rate with 6.7% persistent truants, followed by <a href="/wiki/Fenland_District" title="Fenland District">Fenland</a> (Cambridgeshire) with 6.3%. <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_St_Edmundsbury" title="Borough of St Edmundsbury">St Edmundsbury</a> (Suffolk) has the lowest persistent truancy rate with 2.0%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2016)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>There are twenty seven FE colleges (FECs) in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The largest FE college is <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_New_College" title="Suffolk New College">Suffolk New College</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Young_People%27s_Learning_Agency" title="Young People&#39;s Learning Agency">YPLA</a><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> regional office is based in <a href="/wiki/Stoke,_Suffolk" title="Stoke, Suffolk">Stoke</a>, Ipswich, off the A137 next to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cliff_Quay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cliff Quay (page does not exist)">Cliff Quay</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The main university in the region (and also highly important in England generally) is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The university has been officially rated as the best in the world in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It has the second best medicine course in the world, and in 2010 became the only university outside of the USA to raise over \xc2\xa31 billion in charitable donations.\n</p><p>There are eight universities in the region. Cambridge hosts two universities: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>, which enjoys an international reputation, and <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a>, a vibrant, modern university with an impressive range of undergraduate Degrees, Masters and PhD courses (8 subject areas are rated as \'world-leading\' or \'internationally excellent\' by the government for their research). It is also the home of the <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a>\'s East of England branch. Norwich also hosts two universities: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_East_Anglia" title="University of East Anglia">University of East Anglia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_University_of_the_Arts" title="Norwich University of the Arts">Norwich University of the Arts</a>. There are also other towns and cities in the region which have universities including Bedford and Luton (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Bedfordshire" title="University of Bedfordshire">University of Bedfordshire</a>), Colchester (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Essex" title="University of Essex">University of Essex</a>) and Hatfield (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Hertfordshire" title="University of Hertfordshire">University of Hertfordshire</a>). Other higher education centres in the region include <a href="/wiki/University_Centre_Peterborough" title="University Centre Peterborough">University Centre Peterborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Suffolk" title="University of Suffolk">University of Suffolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Writtle_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Writtle College">Writtle College</a>.\n</p><p>For England, the region has the highest proportion of post-graduate students\xe2\x80\x94thanks mainly to those at Cambridge. Of those undergraduate students studying in the region, around 45% are native to the region\xe2\x80\x94most go elsewhere, and the region is a net exporter of students. Around 40% of the region\'s students are from other regions. The University of Cambridge, due to the high calibre required for entrance, has a mix of students from all over the UK. Around 55% of students in the region come from either the East of England, the South East or London. Very few come from anywhere in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">North of England</a>, especially the <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a> (less than 1%\xe2\x80\x94and most of those will be to Cambridge). Only around 3% come from the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>\xe2\x80\x94a much higher proportion of East of England native students go to study in the East Midlands however.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Essex.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/University_of_Essex.jpg/220px-University_of_Essex.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/University_of_Essex.jpg/330px-University_of_Essex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/University_of_Essex.jpg/440px-University_of_Essex.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Essex.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University of Essex near Colchester</div></div></div>\n<p>The University of Cambridge receives almost three times as much funding as any other university in the region, due to its huge research grant\xe2\x80\x94the largest in England (and the UK). The next largest, by funding, is <a href="/wiki/University_of_East_Anglia" title="University of East Anglia">UEA</a> in Norwich. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Essex" title="University of Essex">University of Essex</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cranfield_University" title="Cranfield University">Cranfield University</a> also have moderately large research grants, but no other universities in the region do. The largest university by student numbers is ARU, and the next biggest is Cambridge. The smallest is Essex.\n</p><p>For total income to universities, Cambridge receives around \xc2\xa31 billion\xe2\x80\x94around six times larger than any other university in the region. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bedfordshire" title="University of Bedfordshire">University of Bedfordshire</a> receives the least income. Cambridge has the lowest drop-out (discontinuation) rate in the region. Once graduated, over 50% of students stay in the region, with 25% going to London and 10% going to the South East. Very few go elsewhere\xe2\x80\x94especially the North of England.\n</p>\n<ul><li>University of Cambridge</li>\n<li>University of East Anglia</li>\n<li>University of Essex</li>\n<li>University of Hertfordshire</li>\n<li>Anglia Ruskin University</li>\n<li>University of Bedfordshire</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The rules of football were largely drawn up by <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Cambridge" title="Trinity College, Cambridge">Trinity College, Cambridge</a> in 1848, known as the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_rules" title="Cambridge rules">Cambridge rules</a> at <a href="/wiki/Parker%27s_Piece" title="Parker&#39;s Piece">Parker\'s Piece</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ebenezer_Cobb_Morley" title="Ebenezer Cobb Morley">Ebenezer Cobb Morley</a> of <a href="/wiki/Barnes_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Barnes Rugby Football Club">Barnes Rugby Football Club</a> in London, also drew up some important rules in 1863, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">Laws of the Game</a></i>.\n</p><p>East of England\'s top representatives in the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a> today are <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a>, who have competed in the top flight at various points.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">Motorsport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Motorsport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/ISport_International" title="ISport International">iSport International</a> is based at <a href="/wiki/Carleton_Rode" title="Carleton Rode">Carleton Rode</a>, south of Norwich in Norfolk. <a href="/wiki/Super_Nova_Racing" title="Super Nova Racing">Super Nova Racing</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Griston" title="Griston">Griston</a>, west of Norwich. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Huff" title="Robert Huff">Robert Huff</a> of Cambridge was the <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Touring_Car_Championship" title="2012 World Touring Car Championship">2012</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Touring_Car_Championship" title="World Touring Car Championship">World Touring Car Championship</a> champion.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rafting">Rafting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rafting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Lee_Valley_White_Water_Centre" title="Lee Valley White Water Centre">Lee Valley White Water Centre</a> is off the <a href="/wiki/A121_road_(England)" title="A121 road (England)">A121</a> in Hertfordshire near <a href="/wiki/Waltham_Cross_railway_station" title="Waltham Cross railway station">Waltham Cross railway station</a>. Peterborough has <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thorpe_Meadows&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thorpe Meadows (page does not exist)">Thorpe Meadows</a> rowing lake.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Orfordness_transmitting_station" title="Orfordness transmitting station">Orfordness transmitting station</a> broadcast the <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a> across Europe on 648&#160;kHz until 2011.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_the_Training_of_Journalists" title="National Council for the Training of Journalists">National Council for the Training of Journalists</a> (NCTJ, important for all journalists) is based near <a href="/wiki/Newport_(Essex)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Newport (Essex) railway station">Newport railway station</a> south of Saffron Walden.\n</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roto_Smeets&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Roto Smeets (page does not exist)">Roto Smeets</a> Ltd (Dutch) is near <a href="/wiki/Sawbridgeworth_railway_station" title="Sawbridgeworth railway station">Sawbridgeworth railway station</a>, actually in <a href="/wiki/Sheering" title="Sheering">Sheering</a> in Essex,and prints the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Express" title="Daily Express">Daily Express</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Star_(British_newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Star (British newspaper)">Daily Star</a></i> magazines.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wyndeham_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wyndeham Group (page does not exist)">Wyndeham Group</a> have main magazine-printing works next to <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_Power_Station" title="Peterborough Power Station">Peterborough Power Station</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Heybridge,_Maldon" title="Heybridge, Maldon">Heybridge, Maldon</a>. Polestar Colchester, off the A123 north of Colchester, formerly printed <i>Nuts</i>, <i>Zoo</i> and <i>Front</i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span
